        <item>
            <title>How to Access Non-Oracle Databases from Autonomous Database using Oracle Database Gateway</title>
            <link>https://blogs.oracle.com/datawarehousing/how-to-access-non-oracle-databases-from-autonomous-database-using-oracle-database-gateway</link>
            <description>&lt;p&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Being able to create database links from Autonomous Database on Shared Infrastructure (ADB-S) to other ADB-S instances or Oracle databases has been one of the most sought-after features that we introduced. ADB-S now supports creating database links to Oracle Database Gateways in order to access non-Oracle databases. In this blog post, we are going to explore how to access a Microsoft SQL Server database from an ADB-S instance using a database link that we will create to a gateway.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Before we jump on the detailed steps, let&amp;rsquo;s do a quick recap of database links in ADB-S. As you may already know, ADB-S requires the target database to be configured with TCP/IP with SSL (TCPS) authentication for outgoing database links since it uses TCPS authentication by default. What this means is that the gateway we want to connect needs to be configured with TCPS authentication as well. We already covered how to configure an Oracle database, such as DBCS, with TCPS authentication in &lt;a href=&quot;https://blogs.oracle.com/datawarehousing/how-to-create-a-database-link-from-an-autonomous-data-warehouse-to-a-database-cloud-service-instance-v2&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;one of my earlier blog posts&lt;/a&gt;. Good news is that configuring Oracle Database Gateway with TCPS is very similar and requires couple minor additional steps. Let&amp;rsquo;s start!&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;The non-Oracle database that I will be using for this demonstration is Microsoft SQL Server 2019 Express running on Windows Server 2019. For simplicity, I chose to install Oracle Database Gateway 19c on the same Windows VM. The installation of the gateway using the Oracle Universal Installer is extremely quick and simple. All you need to provide is a Windows user that has no admin privileges (gateway owner), which non-Oracle database you are planning to connect to and the details of that database such as host name, port number, database name etc. The installer also partially configures a listener for the gateway during the installation and it&amp;rsquo;s possible to choose TCPS authentication in the UI&amp;nbsp;(I will explain what I mean by &amp;#39;partially&amp;#39; in a moment). Here&amp;rsquo;s how my &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;listener.ora&lt;/span&gt; looked like after the installation (note the TCPS protocol in the listener description):&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;


 
# listener.ora Network Configuration File: C:\app\GW\product\19.0.0\tghome_1\NETWORK\ADMIN\listener.ora
# Generated by Oracle configuration tools.

LISTENER =
  (DESCRIPTION_LIST =
    (DESCRIPTION =
      (ADDRESS = (PROTOCOL = TCPS)(HOST = ctuzlaWindows)(PORT = 1522))
    )
  )

SID_LIST_LISTENER = 
  (SID_LIST= 
    (SID_DESC=
      (SID_NAME=dg4msql)
      (GLOBAL_DBNAME=dg4msql_svc)
      (ORACLE_HOME=C:\app\GW\product\19.0.0\tghome_1)
      (PROGRAM=dg4msql)
    ) 
  )


&lt;p&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;In the &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;listener.ora&lt;/span&gt; above, &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;LISTENER&lt;/span&gt; was automatically created by the installer; however, I had to manually add the &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;SID_LIST_LISTENER&lt;/span&gt; variable. It&amp;rsquo;s important to note that &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;SID_NAME&lt;/span&gt; is the SID of the gateway and &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;GLOBAL_DBNAME&lt;/span&gt; is the service name of the gateway. The value of the &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;GLOBAL_DBNAME&lt;/span&gt; variable can be anything you specify and this is the value that we will be using as the target database service name when we create our database link from our Autonomous Database. Additionally, as you can tell from the &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;ORACLE_HOME&lt;/span&gt; path, GW is our Windows user who is also the gateway owner.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Even though our listener already has the TCPS endpoint, we still need to perform couple additional steps so that our ADB-S instance can successfully communicate with the gateway. Here are the steps needed to complete the TCPS configuration in our gateway:&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Create wallets with self signed certificates for server and client&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Exchange certificates between server and client wallets (Export/import certificates)&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Add wallet location in the server network files&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;

&lt;strong&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Create wallets with self signed certificates for server and client&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;As part of enabling TCPS authentication, we need to create individual wallets for the server and the client. Each of these wallets has to have their own certificates that they will exchange with one another. For the sake of this example, I will be using a self signed certificate. The client wallet and certificate can be created in the client side; however, I&amp;#39;ll be creating my client wallet and certificate in the server and moving them to Object Store later on. See &lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/database/oracle/oracle-database/18/dbseg/configuring-secure-sockets-layer-authentication.html#GUID-6AD89576-526F-4D6B-A539-ADF4B840819F&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Configuring Secure Sockets Layer Authentication&lt;/a&gt;&amp;nbsp;for more information. &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;u&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Directories to be used for the wallets and certificates&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;


C:\Users\GW\Desktop\server\wallet
C:\Users\GW\Desktop\client\wallet
C:\Users\GW\Desktop\tmp


&lt;p&gt;&lt;u&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Create a server wallet with the GW user&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;


C:\Users\GW\Desktop\server\wallet&amp;gt;orapki wallet create -wallet ./ -pwd ************ -auto_login
Oracle PKI Tool Release 19.0.0.0.0 - Production
Version 19.3.0.0.0
Copyright (c) 2004, 2019, Oracle and/or its affiliates. All rights reserved.

Operation is successfully completed.


&lt;p&gt;&lt;u&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Create a server certificate with the GW user&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;


C:\Users\GW\Desktop\server\wallet&amp;gt;orapki wallet add -wallet ./ -pwd ************ -dn &amp;quot;CN=windows&amp;quot; -keysize 1024 -self_signed -validity 3650 -sign_alg sha256
Oracle PKI Tool Release 19.0.0.0.0 - Production
Version 19.3.0.0.0
Copyright (c) 2004, 2019, Oracle and/or its affiliates. All rights reserved.

Operation is successfully completed.


&lt;p&gt;&lt;u&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Create a client wallet with the GW user&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;


C:\Users\GW\Desktop\client\wallet&amp;gt;orapki wallet create -wallet ./ -pwd ************ -auto_login
Oracle PKI Tool Release 19.0.0.0.0 - Production
Version 19.3.0.0.0
Copyright (c) 2004, 2019, Oracle and/or its affiliates. All rights reserved.

Operation is successfully completed.


&lt;p&gt;&lt;u&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Create a client certificate with the GW user&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;


C:\Users\GW\Desktop\client\wallet&amp;gt;orapki wallet add -wallet ./ -pwd ************ -dn &amp;quot;CN=ctuzla&amp;quot; -keysize 1024 -self_signed -validity 3650 -sign_alg sha256
Oracle PKI Tool Release 19.0.0.0.0 - Production
Version 19.3.0.0.0
Copyright (c) 2004, 2019, Oracle and/or its affiliates. All rights reserved.

Operation is successfully completed.


&lt;strong&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Exchange certificates between server and client wallets (Export/import certificates)&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;u&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Export the server certificate with the GW user&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;


C:\Users\GW\Desktop\server\wallet&amp;gt;orapki wallet export -wallet ./ -pwd ************ -dn &amp;quot;CN=windows&amp;quot; -cert C:\Users\GW\Desktop\tmp\server.crt
Oracle PKI Tool Release 19.0.0.0.0 - Production
Version 19.3.0.0.0
Copyright (c) 2004, 2019, Oracle and/or its affiliates. All rights reserved.

Operation is successfully completed.


&lt;p&gt;&lt;u&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Export the client certificate with the GW user&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;


C:\Users\GW\Desktop\client\wallet&amp;gt;orapki wallet export -wallet ./ -pwd ************ -dn &amp;quot;CN=ctuzla&amp;quot; -cert C:\Users\GW\Desktop\tmp\client.crt
Oracle PKI Tool Release 19.0.0.0.0 - Production
Version 19.3.0.0.0
Copyright (c) 2004, 2019, Oracle and/or its affiliates. All rights reserved.

Operation is successfully completed.


&lt;p&gt;&lt;u&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Import the client certificate into the server wallet with the GW user&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;


C:\Users\GW\Desktop\server\wallet&amp;gt;orapki wallet add -wallet ./ -pwd ************ -trusted_cert -cert C:\Users\GW\Desktop\tmp\client.crt
Oracle PKI Tool Release 19.0.0.0.0 - Production
Version 19.3.0.0.0
Copyright (c) 2004, 2019, Oracle and/or its affiliates. All rights reserved.

Operation is successfully completed.


&lt;p&gt;&lt;u&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Import the server certificate into the client wallet with the GW user&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;


C:\Users\GW\Desktop\client\wallet&amp;gt;orapki wallet add -wallet ./ -pwd ************ -trusted_cert -cert C:\Users\GW\Desktop\tmp\server.crt
Oracle PKI Tool Release 19.0.0.0.0 - Production
Version 19.3.0.0.0
Copyright (c) 2004, 2019, Oracle and/or its affiliates. All rights reserved.

Operation is successfully completed.


&lt;strong&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Add wallet location in the server network files&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;We now need to modify the server network files so that they point to the server wallet location and they are ready to use the TCPS protocol. Here&amp;#39;s how those files look in my case:&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;u&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Server-side &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;$ORACLE_HOME/network/admin/sqlnet.ora&lt;/span&gt; &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;


 
# sqlnet.ora Network Configuration File: C:\app\GW\product\19.0.0\tghome_1\NETWORK\ADMIN\sqlnet.ora
# Generated by Oracle configuration tools.

SSL_SERVER_DN_MATCH= (ON)

WALLET_LOCATION =
  (SOURCE =
    (METHOD = File)
    (METHOD_DATA =
      (DIRECTORY = C:\Users\GW\Desktop\server\wallet)
    )
  )


&lt;p&gt;&lt;u&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Server-side &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;$ORACLE_HOME/network/admin/listener.ora&lt;/span&gt; &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;


 
# listener.ora Network Configuration File: C:\app\GW\product\19.0.0\tghome_1\NETWORK\ADMIN\listener.ora
# Generated by Oracle configuration tools.

WALLET_LOCATION =
  (SOURCE =
    (METHOD = File)
    (METHOD_DATA =
      (DIRECTORY = C:\Users\GW\Desktop\server\wallet) 
    )
  )

LISTENER =
  (DESCRIPTION_LIST =
    (DESCRIPTION =
      (ADDRESS = (PROTOCOL = TCPS)(HOST = ctuzlaWindows)(PORT = 1522))
    )
  )

SID_LIST_LISTENER = 
  (SID_LIST= 
    (SID_DESC=
      (SID_NAME=dg4msql)
      (GLOBAL_DBNAME=dg4msql_svc)
      (ORACLE_HOME=C:\app\GW\product\19.0.0\tghome_1)
      (PROGRAM=dg4msql)
    ) 
  )


&lt;strong&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Notes About the Target Environment&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;

&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;If your target database is hosted on a Windows VM, make sure the firewall is turned off or configured in a way to not block the incoming traffic.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;As you can see in my listener description above, my listener is configured on port 1522. Since my VM is hosted in OCI, I needed to add an ingress rule for that port that in the security list of my virtual cloud network (VCN). Without this step, I wouldn&amp;rsquo;t be able to reach the listener from my Autonomous Database.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Here&amp;rsquo;s how the HS parameters in my gateway agent init file looks like:&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;


# This is a customized agent init file that contains the HS parameters
# that are needed for the Database Gateway for Microsoft SQL Server
#
# HS init parameters
#
HS_FDS_CONNECT_INFO=ctuzlaWindows:8000//mssfinance
HS_FDS_TRACE_LEVEL=ODBC
HS_FDS_RECOVERY_ACCOUNT=RECOVER
HS_FDS_RECOVERY_PWD=RECOVER


&lt;p style=&quot;margin-left:40px&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Please note that my SQL Server database (&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;mssfinance&lt;/span&gt;) is configured to have TCP enabled on port 8000 as shown above.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Confirm the listener status:&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;


C:\Users\GW&amp;gt;lsnrctl status

LSNRCTL for 64-bit Windows: Version 19.0.0.0.0 - Production on 24-JUL-2020 09:27:30

Copyright (c) 1991, 2019, Oracle.  All rights reserved.

Connecting to (DESCRIPTION=(ADDRESS=(PROTOCOL=TCPS)(HOST=ctuzlaWindows)(PORT=1522)))
STATUS of the LISTENER
------------------------
Alias                     LISTENER
Version                   TNSLSNR for 64-bit Windows: Version 19.0.0.0.0 - Production
Start Date                17-JUL-2020 20:35:35
Uptime                    6 days 12 hr. 51 min. 59 sec
Trace Level               off
Security                  ON: Local OS Authentication
SNMP                      OFF
Listener Parameter File   C:\app\GW\product\19.0.0\tghome_1\network\admin\listener.ora
Listener Log File         C:\app\GW\diag\tnslsnr\ctuzlaWindows\listener\alert\log.xml
Listening Endpoints Summary...
  (DESCRIPTION=(ADDRESS=(PROTOCOL=tcps)(HOST=ctuzlaWindows)(PORT=1522)))
Services Summary...
Service &amp;quot;dg4msql_svc&amp;quot; has 1 instance(s).
  Instance &amp;quot;dg4msql&amp;quot;, status UNKNOWN, has 1 handler(s) for this service...
The command completed successfully


&lt;strong&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Create a Database Link from ADB-S to the Gateway&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;We now have a working TCPS authentication in the gateway. Here are the steps from the &lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/paas/autonomous-data-warehouse-cloud/user/database-links-other-databases.html#GUID-E4F35EEE-3147-4822-A9EB-A341D87E4ECF&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;documentation&lt;/a&gt;&amp;nbsp;that we will follow to create a database link from ADB-S to the gateway:&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Copy the client wallet (&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;cwallet.sso&lt;/span&gt;) that we created in &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;C:\Users\GW\Desktop\client\wallet&lt;/span&gt; to Object Store.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Create credentials to access your Object Store where you store the &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;cwallet.sso&lt;/span&gt;. See &lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/paas/autonomous-data-warehouse-cloud/user/dbms-cloud.html#GUID-742FC365-AA09-48A8-922C-1987795CF36A&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;CREATE_CREDENTIAL Procedure&lt;/a&gt; for details.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Create a directory to store the target database wallet:&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;


SQL&amp;gt; create directory wallet_dir as &amp;#39;walletdir&amp;#39;;

Directory WALLET_DIR created.


&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Upload the wallet to the &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;wallet_dir&lt;/span&gt; directory on ADB-S using &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;DBMS_CLOUD.GET_OBJECT&lt;/span&gt;:&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;


SQL&amp;gt; BEGIN
  DBMS_CLOUD.GET_OBJECT(
    credential_name =&amp;gt; &amp;#39;OBJ_STORE_CRED&amp;#39;,
    object_uri =&amp;gt; &amp;#39;https://objectstorage.us-phoenix-1.oraclecloud.com/n/adbstraining/b/target-wallet/o/cwallet.sso&amp;#39;,
    directory_name =&amp;gt; &amp;#39;WALLET_DIR&amp;#39;); 
END;
/    
 
PL/SQL procedure successfully completed.


&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;On ADB-S, create credentials to access the target database. The username and password you specify with &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;DBMS_CLOUD.CREATE_CREDENTIAL&lt;/span&gt; are the credentials for the target database that you use to create the database link:&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;


BEGIN
  DBMS_CLOUD.CREATE_CREDENTIAL(
    credential_name =&amp;gt; &amp;#39;SSFINANCE_LINK_CRED&amp;#39;,
    username =&amp;gt; &amp;#39;mssadmin&amp;#39;,
    password =&amp;gt; &amp;#39;************&amp;#39;);
END;
/ 

PL/SQL procedure successfully completed.


&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Create the database link to the target database using &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;DBMS_CLOUD_ADMIN.CREATE_DATABASE_LINK&lt;/span&gt;:&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;


BEGIN
     DBMS_CLOUD_ADMIN.CREATE_DATABASE_LINK(
          db_link_name =&amp;gt; &amp;#39;FINANCELINK&amp;#39;, 
          hostname =&amp;gt; &amp;#39;149.343.90.113&amp;#39;, 
          port =&amp;gt; &amp;#39;1522&amp;#39;,
          service_name =&amp;gt; &amp;#39;dg4msql_svc&amp;#39;,
          ssl_server_cert_dn =&amp;gt; &amp;#39;CN=windows&amp;#39;,
          credential_name =&amp;gt; &amp;#39;SSFINANCE_LINK_CRED&amp;#39;,
          directory_name =&amp;gt; &amp;#39;WALLET_DIR&amp;#39;,
          gateway_link =&amp;gt; TRUE);
END;
/

PL/SQL procedure successfully completed.


&lt;p style=&quot;margin-left: 40px;&quot;&gt;Note that&amp;nbsp;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;DBMS_CLOUD_ADMIN.CREATE_DATABASE_LINK&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;procedure has a new parameter called&amp;nbsp;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;gateway_link&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&amp;nbsp;that needs to be set to&amp;nbsp;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;TRUE&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt; when creating a database link to an Oracle Database Gateway.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li style=&quot;margin-right:24px; margin-bottom:2px&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;background:white&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;color:black&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;line-height:18.0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:&amp;quot;Oracle Sans&amp;quot;,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Use the database link you created to access the data on the target database:&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;


select count(*) from CUSTOMERS@FINANCELINK;

COUNT(*)
--------
4


&lt;p&gt;This&amp;nbsp;is all you need in order to access a non-Oracle database from your Autonomous Database! In this post, we have gone through gateway installation, TCPS configuration in gateways, target environment tips and database link creation in order to access a SQL Server database. The same steps apply to other non-Oracle databases that are supported by Oracle Database Gateway as well.&lt;/p&gt;
</description>

            <pubDate>Fri, 24 Jul 2020 15:44:00 +0000</pubDate>

        </item>
        <item>
            <title>Using OCI Resource Manage to deploy a complete end-to-end data warehouse</title>
            <link>https://blogs.oracle.com/datawarehousing/using-oci-resource-manage-to-deploy-a-complete-end-to-end-data-warehouse</link>
            <description>A while back, I announced in the &lt;a href=&quot;https://blogs.oracle.com/datawarehousing/newsletter&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Autonomous Database Newsletter&lt;/a&gt; (&lt;a href=&quot;https://blogs.oracle.com/datawarehousing/autonomous-database-newsletter-june-24-2020#rap&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;June 24 edition&lt;/a&gt;) that we now had a series of reference architecture patterns for Autonomous Data Warehouse. Currently, the following patterns are available (&lt;em&gt;note: more patterns are being built and will be added shortly&lt;/em&gt;):
&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/solutions/oci-ebs-analysis/index.html&quot; name=&quot;cta=External Link Click&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Departmental data warehousing - an EBS integration example&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/solutions/oci-spreadsheet-analysis/index.html&quot; name=&quot;cta=External Link Click&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Departmental data warehousing/data marts - consolidate spreadsheets&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/solutions/oci-curated-analysis/index.html&quot; name=&quot;cta=External Link Click&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Enterprise data warehousing - an integrated data lake example&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/solutions/data-science-environment/index.html#GUID-CE4B3020-881C-481D-B434-199388C3ADD3&quot; name=&quot;cta=External Link Click&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Set up a data science environment that uses Oracle Machine Learning&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Each reference architecture pattern comes&amp;nbsp;with the following: best practices framework; a set of recommendations which are a starting point for implementing the pattern and a terraform script for deploying the end-to-end set of cloud services on OCI. That was great news for everyone because you now had a very precise system architecture&amp;nbsp;plan for each data warehouse use case that could be expanded to incorporate additional use cases as your data warehouse project evolved over time.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;These patterns were the result of a some amazing work by our Enterprise Architecture, OCI andADB PM teams. There are a lot more patterns to come and I will let you know as new ones get added to the list.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;I have used a couple of the patterns myself and, if I am honest, while the Terraform scripts are great it was hard work to setup all the required keys etc and get everything in to place so I could run one of the pre-built Terraform scripts. But then again, Terraform is a completely new area for me!&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Then this week our OCI team announced they have&amp;nbsp;added one of our data warehouse patterns to the list of pre-built stacks within &lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.cloud.oracle.com/en-us/iaas/Content/ResourceManager/Concepts/resourcemanager.htm&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;OCI Resource Manager&lt;/a&gt;. Here&amp;#39;s a screen grab of the list of built-in stacks that are ready for deploying:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/b98a78434d7507df090d0fbfc44302cd/screenshot_2020_07_23_at_12_46_38.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 600px; height: 247px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Right now, we have the &amp;quot;Departmental Data Warehouse&amp;quot; pattern available as a stack and this deploys an instance of Autonomous Database and an instance on Oracle Analytics Cloud for you. So how do you get started? Here is a walk-through of the main screens:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Step 1) - I have logged into my Always Free cloud account and arrived at the main OCI home page:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/68f29f2ced7bc0d11f6ad7e5471bf249/slide1.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 600px; height: 338px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Step 2 - I have opened the main menu tree and scrolled down to &lt;strong&gt;Resource Manager&lt;/strong&gt; and then selected &amp;quot;&lt;strong&gt;Stacks&lt;/strong&gt;&amp;quot;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/41f4e9da371740898a33d223843c8f30/slide5.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 600px; height: 338px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Step 3 - As this is the first stack I have built my home page is currently empty. Obviously we click on the blue &lt;strong&gt;Create Stack&lt;/strong&gt; button.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/7477f491200093737cd643432c6eb7d4/slide7.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 600px; height: 338px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Step 4 - I can build my own stack deployment process or I can select to use a pre-built stack and this is what we need to use in this case...&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/71b9a2c6d2de83d89a335ed3fa966bf0/slide9.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 600px; height: 338px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Step 5 - this pops a form which lists all the available pre-built stacks as I showed above. In this case I want to build a departmental data warehouse so let&amp;#39;s select that box&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/831bf7ad0111e7b6db0784ab4ad2a6c9/slide11.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 600px; height: 338px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Step 6 - now I can set the name and description for my deployment &amp;quot;stack&amp;quot; along with the compartment I want to use in my deployment (if you are not sure what a compartment is or does then spend a few minutes looking at &lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.cloud.oracle.com/en-us/iaas/Content/Identity/Tasks/managingcompartments.htm&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;this page&lt;/a&gt; in the documentation). Once you are happy with the information on this page, click the &lt;strong&gt;Next&lt;/strong&gt; button in the bottom left corner.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/d42fe51cfd735ef5080fc8fec0e0fefd/slide14.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 600px; height: 338px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Step 7 - this brings us to the form which is going to capture the information about our ADW and OAC instances. In the screen below you can see that I have set the number of CPUs for my ADW instance as 1, I have set the password for my ADMIN user, I have changed the name and display name for my new database, I have elected to build a 19c autonomous data warehouse and I have enabled auto-scaling. For storage, I am going to start with 1 TB. Just point out....both the number of OCPUs and the amount of storage and can be scaled independently and with zero downtime.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/2a83aa6199c907a77330ff5d4c47c025/slide20.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 600px; height: 338px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Step 8 - scrolling down....I can set my license type. We allow you to bring your on-premise licenses to the cloud or you can simply buy additional licenses as required. With this departmental warehouse project I know I am going to include personally identifiable information about some of our&amp;nbsp;employees so I need to keep that data totally safe and secure. Therefore, I am going to register my ADW instance with our &lt;a href=&quot;https://www.oracle.com/database/technologies/security/data-safe.html&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Data Safe&lt;/a&gt; service (which is free to use with Autonomous Database).&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/275caec9b7044069460b2342b4534589/slide26.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 600px; height: 338px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;...and to further protect my ADW instance this pre-built stack automatically uses Access Control Lists (ACLs). If you want more information about to use ACLs then &lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/paas/autonomous-data-warehouse-cloud/user/security-restrict-acl.html#GUID-90E6CF76-E6C4-4B7E-B424-91DBB35DFE0F&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;. This process within Resource Manager will automatically configure the ACLs so that OAC can connect to my ADW instance so that&amp;#39;s all taken care of but I need to allow my desktop computer to access my ADW instance as well. Therefore, I have to enter the public IP address for my desktop computer. If you don&amp;#39;t include this information then you will not be able to use any of the desktop tools or built-in tools that come with ADW.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Step 9 - &amp;nbsp;Setup the details for my OAC instance. Again, I have opted for 1 OCPU and I am going to take&amp;nbsp;the ENTERPRISE_ANALYTICS deployment option since this gives me access to all the features I need. If you use the pulldown menu you will there are two options: 1)Self-service analytics deploys an instance with data visualization,&amp;nbsp;and 2)&amp;nbsp;Enterprise analytics deploys an instance with enterprise modeling, reporting, and data visualization.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/96b3e8236835bc559cab53f2b4ed82e8/slide28.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 600px; height: 338px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Step 10 - and now we are at the end of the process and ready to deploy our end-to-end departmental data warehouse. The review page gives us a chance to make sure everything is correct before we hit the &lt;strong&gt;Create&lt;/strong&gt;&amp;nbsp;button.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/43bd65d130076ced63f40237b99a1cd3/slide30.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 600px; height: 338px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;The &lt;strong&gt;Jobs&lt;/strong&gt;&amp;nbsp;tab allows you to monitor progress of your deployment and at the end of this process you should have a new ADW instance and a new OAC instance within your tenancy. &amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;strong&gt;Congratulations&lt;/strong&gt;

&lt;p&gt;You should now have your new departmental data warehouse ready for use,&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;strong&gt;What&amp;#39;s Next&lt;/strong&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Next you can start loading data into your ADW instance. Take a look at the Chapter&amp;nbsp;3 in the ADW documentation which covers loading data with Autonomous Data Warehouse -&amp;nbsp;&lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/paas/autonomous-data-warehouse-cloud/user/load-data.html#GUID-1351807C-E3F7-4C6D-AF83-2AEEADE2F83E&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/paas/autonomous-data-warehouse-cloud/user/load-data.html#GUID-1351807C-E3F7-4C6D-AF83-2AEEADE2F83E&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Then you can launch the Oracle Analytics home page in your browser, connect to your ADW instance and start building reports and dashboards.&amp;nbsp;The OAC product management team has put together a great series of labs that will get you started with OAC and ADW, see here:&amp;nbsp;&lt;a href=&quot;https://www.oracle.com/uk/business-analytics/data-visualization/tutorials.html&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;https://www.oracle.com/uk/business-analytics/data-visualization/tutorials.html&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Hope this was useful and I will let you know as we add more patterns to the solution library and more patterns into the pre-built stacks within OCI Resource Manager.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

            <title>Autonomous Database Newsletter - July 22 2020</title>

            <description>

						&lt;div style=&quot;margin-left:20px; margin-right:20px; color:#000000; text-align: left; font-family: Helvetica, Arial, sans-serif; height:170px&quot;&gt;
							&lt;br&gt;
							&lt;span style=&quot;margin-left:20px; font-size:25pt; line-height:1.5;&quot;&gt;Autonomous Database&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br&gt;
							&lt;span style=&quot;margin-left:20px; font-size:15pt; line-height:1.5;&quot;&gt;on Shared Exadata Infrastructure&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br&gt;
							&lt;span style=&quot;margin-left:20px; font-size:12pt; line-height:1.5;&quot;&gt;July 22, 2020&lt;/span&gt;
						&lt;/div&gt;
					
				
			
			&lt;a name=&quot;btt&quot;&gt;&lt;/a&gt;

			
				
					
						
						&lt;div style=&quot;margin-left:20px;&quot;&gt;&amp;nbsp;
						&lt;p&gt;Welcome to our latest customer newsletter for Autonomous Database on Shared Exadata Infrastructure.&amp;nbsp;This newsletter covers the following new features and topics:&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;ul&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;#gwno&quot; style=&quot;color: grey !important;&quot;&gt;Using Autonomous Data Guard&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;#mdwp&quot; style=&quot;color: grey !important;&quot;&gt;MDW Patterns in OCI Resource Manager&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
						&lt;/ul&gt;

						&lt;p style=&quot;font-style: italic; font-family:Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; font-size:14px; color:#000000;&quot;&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Note:&lt;/strong&gt; some new features are only available with &lt;strong&gt;19c&lt;/strong&gt;. To get the most from Autonomous Database, upgrade to 19c as soon as possible. There is more information about how to upgrade existing 18c instances to 19c &lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/paas/autonomous-data-warehouse-cloud/user/autonomous-upgrade.html#GUID-47F4EA0B-C4B6-4135-A284-AE730D550F1C&quot; style=&quot;color: grey !important;&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt; here, for ADW&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/paas/atp-cloud/atpug/autonomous-upgrade.html#GUID-47F4EA0B-C4B6-4135-A284-AE730D550F1C&quot; style=&quot;color: grey !important;&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;here, for ATP&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;Don&amp;#39;t forget to checkout our &lt;strong&gt;&amp;quot;What&amp;#39;s New&amp;quot;&lt;/strong&gt; page for a comprehensive archive of all the new features we have added to Autonomous Database - &lt;a href=&quot;https://www.oracle.com/database/technologies/datawarehouse-bigdata/adw-features.html&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;To find out how to subscribe to this newsletter &lt;a href=&quot;https://blogs.oracle.com/datawarehousing/announcing-customer-newsletter-for-autonomous-database&quot; style=&quot;color: grey !important;&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
						&lt;/div&gt;
						
						&amp;nbsp;
					
				
			
			&lt;a name=&quot;gwno&quot;&gt;&lt;/a&gt;

			
				
					
						
						&lt;div style=&quot;margin-left:10px;&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;Icon for creating a standby dataabase&quot; moz-do-not-send=&quot;true&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/bb422732717be7b5766701bad5c22ac4/replication.png&quot; /&gt;
						&lt;p class=&quot;serverless&quot;&gt;(Shared&lt;br /&gt;
						Infrastructure&lt;br /&gt;
						Only)&lt;/p&gt;
						&lt;/div&gt;
						
						&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;span style=&quot;font-weight:bold; color:red;&quot;&gt;NEW &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;feature_header&quot;&gt; - Creating a Standby Database with ADG&lt;/span&gt;
						&lt;p class=&quot;basic_text&quot;&gt;When you enable Autonomous Data Guard on ADB, the system creates a standby database that stays &amp;quot;connected&amp;quot; to the primary database and automatically refreshes its data from the primary database.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p class=&quot;basic_text&quot;&gt;This allows the following, depending on the state of the primary database:&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p class=&quot;basic_text&quot; style=&quot;margin-left:55px;&quot;&gt;If your primary database goes down, Autonomous Data Guard converts the standby database to the primary database with minimal interruption. After failover completes, Autonomous Data Guard automatically creates a new standby database.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p class=&quot;basic_text&quot; style=&quot;margin-left:55px;&quot;&gt;You can perform a switchover operation, where the primary database becomes the standby database, and the standby database becomes the primary database.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p class=&quot;basic_text&quot;&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Note:&lt;/strong&gt; Autonomous Database does not provide access to the standby database.&lt;/p&gt;
						&lt;img alt=&quot;Simplified animated GIF showing creation of an Autonomous Data Guard standby instance for ADW&quot; id=&quot;myImg&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/3f425d604e4ec4fb55c3b40f8f72b98e/adg_animation.gif&quot; style=&quot;width:100%;max-width:550px&quot; /&gt; 
						&lt;div class=&quot;modal&quot; id=&quot;myModal&quot;&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;close&quot;&gt;&amp;times;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;img class=&quot;modal-content&quot; id=&quot;img01&quot; /&gt;
						&lt;div class=&quot;caption&quot; id=&quot;caption&quot;&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/div&gt;
						&lt;/div&gt;
						
// Get the modal
var modal = document.getElementById(&quot;myModal&quot;);

// Get the image and insert it inside the modal - use its &quot;alt&quot; text as a caption
var img = document.getElementById(&quot;myImg&quot;);
var modalImg = document.getElementById(&quot;img01&quot;);
var captionText = document.getElementById(&quot;caption&quot;);
img.onclick = function(){
  modal.style.display = &quot;block&quot;;
  modalImg.src = this.src;
  captionText.innerHTML = this.alt;
}

// Get the &lt;span&gt; element that closes the modal
var span = document.getElementsByClassName(&quot;close&quot;)[0];

// When the user clicks on &lt;span&gt; (x), close the modal
span.onclick = function() { 
  modal.style.display = &quot;none&quot;;
}

						&lt;div style=&quot;margin-left:20px; margin-right:20px; color:#000000; text-align: left; font-family: Helvetica, Arial, sans-serif; height:170px&quot;&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;span style=&quot;margin-left:20px; font-size:25pt; line-height:1.5;&quot;&gt;Autonomous Database&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;span style=&quot;margin-left:20px; font-size:15pt; line-height:1.5;&quot;&gt;on Shared Exadata Infrastructure&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;span style=&quot;margin-left:20px; font-size:12pt; line-height:1.5;&quot;&gt;July 15, 2020&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
						
					
				
			
&lt;a name=&quot;btt&quot;&gt;&lt;/a&gt;
			
				
					
						
						&lt;div style=&quot;margin-left:20px;&quot;&gt;&amp;nbsp;
						&lt;p&gt;Welcome to our latest customer newsletter for Autonomous Database on Shared Exadata Infrastructure.&amp;nbsp;This newsletter covers the following new features and topics:&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;ul&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;#gwno&quot; style=&quot;color: grey !important;&quot;&gt;Connecting to non-Oracle Databases&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;#mncs&quot; style=&quot;color: grey !important;&quot;&gt;Modify Network Configuration&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;#tzfs&quot; style=&quot;color: grey !important;&quot;&gt;Timezone Support&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;#mupp&quot; style=&quot;color: grey !important;&quot;&gt;Modifying User Profiles&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;#gsgs&quot; style=&quot;color: grey !important;&quot;&gt;Updated Quick Start Guides&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;#apex&quot; style=&quot;color: grey !important;&quot;&gt;APEX 20.1 is coming to ADB&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;#dwgl&quot; style=&quot;color: grey !important;&quot;&gt;Global Leaders Update&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
						&lt;/ul&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;Don&amp;#39;t forget to checkout our &lt;strong&gt;&amp;quot;What&amp;#39;s New&amp;quot;&lt;/strong&gt; page for a comprehensive archive of all the new features we have added to Autonomous Database - &lt;a href=&quot;https://www.oracle.com/database/technologies/datawarehouse-bigdata/adw-features.html&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;To find out how to subscribe to this newsletter &lt;a href=&quot;https://blogs.oracle.com/datawarehousing/announcing-customer-newsletter-for-autonomous-database&quot; style=&quot;color: grey !important;&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
						&lt;/div&gt;
						
						&amp;nbsp;
					
				
			
			&lt;a name=&quot;gwno&quot;&gt;&lt;/a&gt;

			
				
					
						
						&lt;div style=&quot;margin-left:10px;&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;Icon for ADB Connecting to non-Oracle Databases Using Gateways&quot; moz-do-not-send=&quot;true&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/5195072cc786ce37fa0dd61c219d885f/evolution_1of5.png&quot; /&gt;
						&lt;p class=&quot;serverless&quot;&gt;(Shared&lt;br /&gt;
						Infrastructure&lt;br /&gt;
						Only)&lt;/p&gt;
						&lt;/div&gt;
						
						&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;span style=&quot;font-weight:bold; color:red;&quot;&gt;NEW &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;feature_header&quot;&gt; - Connecting to Non-Oracle Databases&lt;/span&gt;
						&lt;p class=&quot;basic_text&quot;&gt;Autonomous Database now supports using connections that are enabled via Oracle Database Gateway. Gateways are designed for accessing a specific non-Oracle Database such as DB2, Teradata, SQL Server etc.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p class=&quot;basic_text&quot;&gt;Oracle Database Gateway provide queries and applications with access to data anywhere in a distributed database system without knowing either the location of the data or how it is stored. This removes the need to customize applications to access data from non-Oracle systems.&lt;/p&gt;
						&amp;nbsp;

						
							
								
									LEARN MORE
								
							
						

						
							
								
									
									&lt;div class=&quot;row_set&quot;&gt;
									&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

									&lt;p class=&quot;basic_text&quot;&gt;DOC: Create Database Links to an Oracle Database Gateway to Access Non-Oracle Databases (ADW), &lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/paas/autonomous-data-warehouse-cloud/user/database-links-other-databases.html#GUID-E4F35EEE-3147-4822-A9EB-A341D87E4ECF&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;

									&lt;p class=&quot;basic_text&quot;&gt;DOC: Create Database Links to an Oracle Database Gateway to Access Non-Oracle Databases (ATP), &lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/paas/atp-cloud/atpug/database-links-other-databases.html#GUID-E4F35EEE-3147-4822-A9EB-A341D87E4ECF&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;

									&lt;p class=&quot;basic_text&quot;&gt;DOC: Introduction to Heterogeneous Connectivity, &lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/database/oracle/oracle-database/19/heter/introduction.html#GUID-EC402025-0CC0-401F-AF93-888B8A3089FE&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;

									&lt;p class=&quot;basic_text&quot;&gt;DOC: Install guides for Database Gateways, &lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/database/oracle/oracle-database/19/distributed-data.html&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
									&lt;/div&gt;
									
								
							
						
						&amp;nbsp;

						&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;
						
						&amp;nbsp;
					
				
			

			
				
					
						&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;a class=&quot;btt&quot; href=&quot;#btt&quot;&gt;BACK TO TOP&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
						&amp;nbsp;
					
				
			
			&lt;a name=&quot;mncs&quot;&gt;&lt;/a&gt;

			
				
					
						
						&lt;div style=&quot;margin-left:10px;&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;Icon for ADB network settings&quot; moz-do-not-send=&quot;true&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/e84fe50993ddf49d462eee5d11219ba8/cloud_utilities_blue.png&quot; /&gt;
						&lt;p class=&quot;serverless&quot;&gt;(Shared&lt;br /&gt;
						Infrastructure&lt;br /&gt;
						Only)&lt;/p&gt;
						&lt;/div&gt;
						
						&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;span style=&quot;font-weight:bold; color:red;&quot;&gt;NEW &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;feature_header&quot;&gt; - Modify Network Settings for ADB Instances&lt;/span&gt;
						&lt;p class=&quot;basic_text&quot;&gt;Autonomous Database now supports switching network access type. This feature enables customers to perform an in-place switch from public endpoint to private endpoint (and vice versa).&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;br /&gt;
						The feature will reduce customer effort required for switching between public and private endpoints and make it easier for customers to adopt private endpoint.&lt;/p&gt;
						&amp;nbsp;

						&lt;div class=&quot;row&quot;&gt;

			&lt;a name=&quot;tzfs&quot;&gt;&lt;/a&gt;

			
				
					
						
						&lt;div style=&quot;margin-left:10px;&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;Icon for timezone files for autonomous database&quot; moz-do-not-send=&quot;true&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/ac4dd626a1f5421a914b1c8aaffd0440/clock_24_7_512.png&quot; /&gt;
						&lt;p class=&quot;serverless&quot;&gt;(Shared&lt;br /&gt;
						Infrastructure&lt;br /&gt;
						Only)&lt;/p&gt;
						&lt;/div&gt;
						
						&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;span style=&quot;font-weight:bold; color:red;&quot;&gt;NEW &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;feature_header&quot;&gt; - Timezone Files Automatically Updated&lt;/span&gt;
						&lt;p class=&quot;basic_text&quot;&gt;For time zone support, Oracle Database uses time zone files that store the list of all time zones. The time zone files for Autonomous Database are periodically updated to reflect the latest time zone specific changes.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p class=&quot;basic_text&quot;&gt;An Autonomous Database instance will automatically pick up updated time zone files depending on the lifecycle state of the instance:&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p class=&quot;basic_text&quot; style=&quot;margin-left:45px;&quot;&gt;- Stopped: At the next start operation the update is automatically applied.&lt;br /&gt;
						- Available: After a restart the update is automatically applied.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p class=&quot;basic_text&quot;&gt;When a load or import operation results in a timezone related error, restart the ADB instance and try again.&lt;/p&gt;
						&amp;nbsp;

						
							
								
									LEARN MORE
								
							
						

						
							
								
									
									&lt;div class=&quot;row_set&quot;&gt;&amp;nbsp;
									&lt;p class=&quot;basic_text&quot;&gt;DOC: Manage Time Zone Data Updates on ADW, &lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/paas/autonomous-data-warehouse-cloud/user/event-notification.html#GUID-BACC9C4A-C0FA-4912-862A-1A2A24D6A0C2&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;

									&lt;p class=&quot;basic_text&quot;&gt;DOC: Manage Time Zone Data Updates on ATP, &lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/paas/atp-cloud/atpug/event-notification.html#GUID-BACC9C4A-C0FA-4912-862A-1A2A24D6A0C2&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;

									&lt;p class=&quot;basic_text&quot;&gt;EINSTEIN: How Does Time Zone Upgrade Work in Autonomous Database on Shared Exadata Infrastructure (ADB-S), &lt;a href=&quot;https://einstein.oracle.com/apex/f?p=EINSTEIN:Q:8154983712774:::10:QUESTION:how-does-time-zone-upgrade-work-in-autonomous-database-on-s-3233&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;

			&lt;a name=&quot;mupp&quot;&gt;&lt;/a&gt;

			
				
					
						
						&lt;div style=&quot;margin-left:10px;&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;Icon for added security through user profiles and option to set password verification&quot; moz-do-not-send=&quot;true&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/4a4156c51124dac49aa37df2119cb9b2/security.png&quot; /&gt;
						&lt;p class=&quot;serverless&quot;&gt;(Shared&lt;br /&gt;
						Infrastructure&lt;br /&gt;
						Only)&lt;/p&gt;
						&lt;/div&gt;
						
						&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;span style=&quot;font-weight:bold; color:red;&quot;&gt;NEW &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;feature_header&quot;&gt; - Create/Modify User Profile and Set Password Rules&lt;/span&gt;
						&lt;p class=&quot;basic_text&quot;&gt;Autonomous Database now supports the ability to create/alter user profiles and import existing user profiles from another environment with Oracle Data Pump Import.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p class=&quot;basic_text&quot;&gt;Cloud Admins can now manage the rules for password complexity on Autonomous Database. Administrators can can create a Password Verify Function (PVF) and associate the PVF with a profile to manage the rules for password complexity.&lt;/p&gt;

			&lt;a name=&quot;btt&quot;&gt;&lt;/a&gt;

			
				
					
						
						&lt;div style=&quot;margin-left:20px;&quot;&gt;&amp;nbsp;
						&lt;p&gt;Welcome to our latest customer newsletter for Autonomous Database on Shared Exadata Infrastructure.&amp;nbsp;This newsletter covers the following new features and topics:&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;ul&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;#orc&quot; style=&quot;color: grey !important;&quot;&gt;Support for ORC files&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;#19c&quot; style=&quot;color: grey !important;&quot;&gt;Automatic upgrade to 19c&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;#awr&quot; style=&quot;color: grey !important;&quot;&gt;AWR Reports in Performance Hub&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;#ftl&quot; style=&quot;color: grey !important;&quot;&gt;Changes to file transfer limits into Object Store&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;#ras&quot; style=&quot;color: grey !important;&quot;&gt;Procedures for using Database Real Application Security&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;#rap&quot; style=&quot;color: grey !important;&quot;&gt;Reference architecture patterns for data warehousing&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
						&lt;/ul&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;Don&amp;#39;t forget to checkout our &lt;strong&gt;&amp;quot;What&amp;#39;s New&amp;quot;&lt;/strong&gt; page for a comprehensive archive of all the new features we have added to Autonomous Database - &lt;a href=&quot;https://www.oracle.com/database/technologies/datawarehouse-bigdata/adw-features.html&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;To find out how to subscribe to this newsletter &lt;a href=&quot;https://blogs.oracle.com/datawarehousing/announcing-customer-newsletter-for-autonomous-database&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
						&lt;/div&gt;
						
						&amp;nbsp;
					
				
			
			&lt;a name=&quot;orc&quot;&gt;&lt;/a&gt;

			
				
					
						
						&lt;div style=&quot;margin-left:10px;&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;ADB Support for ORC files&quot; moz-do-not-send=&quot;true&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/7850eb5d39dcbb79b110d1deea442d81/apex_logo.jpg&quot; /&gt;
						&lt;p class=&quot;serverless&quot;&gt;(Shared&lt;br /&gt;
						Infrastructure&lt;br /&gt;
						Only)&lt;/p&gt;
						&lt;/div&gt;
						
						&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;span style=&quot;font-weight:bold; color:red;&quot;&gt;NEW &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;feature_header&quot;&gt; - ADB now supports ORC files&lt;/span&gt;
						&lt;p&gt;ADB has expanded object storage support in two important ways: it can now query &lt;a href=&quot;https://cwiki.apache.org/confluence/display/Hive/LanguageManual+ORC&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;ORC files&lt;/a&gt; as well as complex data types found in Parquet, ORC and Avro files.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p style=&quot;margin-left:25px; font-style:italic;&quot;&gt;The Optimized Row Columnar (ORC) file is a highly efficient way to store Hive data. It was designed to overcome limitations of the other Hive file formats. Like Parquet, ORC data is stored in a compressed columnar format and provides metadata to enable efficient reads.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;ORC, Parquet and Avro file types provide the ability to capture fields containing complex data types, including arrays, maps, unions and objects (or structs). These complex types can now be queried in ADB using Oracle&amp;rsquo;s extensive JSON query support.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Note&lt;/strong&gt;: support for ORC and complex data types are only available in 19c.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
						&amp;nbsp;

						
							
								
									LEARN MORE

			&lt;a name=&quot;19c&quot;&gt;&lt;/a&gt;

			
				
					
						
						&lt;div style=&quot;margin-left:10px;&quot;&gt;&lt;img moz-do-not-send=&quot;true&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/7452caec8faf22b604482d875395e694/19c_logo.png&quot; /&gt;

						&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;span style=&quot;font-weight:bold; color:red;&quot;&gt;NOTE&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;feature_header&quot;&gt; - Customer Announcement About Automatic Upgrade to 19c&lt;/span&gt;
						&lt;p&gt;An email announcement about the automatic upgrade to Database 19c has been sent to ADB customers (&lt;em&gt;see below&lt;/em&gt;). The automatic upgrade of Autonomous Databases will start in September.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;At the date of the scheduled upgrade, Autonomous Database instances will be automatically upgraded in-place to Oracle Database 19c.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;Please note that to better manage the customer experience during this upgrade process we are recommending that customers contact support by logging a service request if they have any questions about the upgrade process.&lt;/p&gt;
						&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;img alt=&quot;Email message for Autonomous Database automatic upgrade to 19c&quot; moz-do-not-send=&quot;true&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/8667439a639aa900e4e4c19aa4d8a11a/upgrade_19c_550.png&quot; /&gt;
						&lt;p&gt;To view the options for manually upgrading an exsting ADW instance to Database 19c - &lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/paas/autonomous-data-warehouse-cloud/user/autonomous-upgrade.html#GUID-47F4EA0B-C4B6-4135-A284-AE730D550F1C&quot; style=&quot;color: grey !important;&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;To view the options for manually upgrading an exsting ATP instance to Database 19c - &lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/paas/atp-cloud/atpug/autonomous-upgrade.html#GUID-47F4EA0B-C4B6-4135-A284-AE730D550F1C&quot; style=&quot;color: grey !important;&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
						&lt;br /&gt;

			&lt;a name=&quot;awr&quot;&gt;&lt;/a&gt;

			
				
					
						
						&lt;div style=&quot;margin-left:10px;&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;Icon for AWR Reports on Performance Hub&quot; moz-do-not-send=&quot;true&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/7262f9add7a1acfa96751223c00098ab/psb.png&quot; /&gt;
						&lt;p class=&quot;serverless&quot;&gt;(Shared&lt;br /&gt;
						Infrastructure&lt;br /&gt;
						Only)&lt;/p&gt;
						&lt;/div&gt;
						
						&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;span style=&quot;font-weight:bold; color:red;&quot;&gt;NEW &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;feature_header&quot;&gt; - Download AWR Reports From Performance Hub&lt;/span&gt;
						&lt;p&gt;Automatic Workload Repository (AWR) report is a vital tool to collect historical performance statistics of an Oracle Database by DBAs and System Performance engineers.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;Performance Hub on the OCI console now allows customers to download an AWR report for a specific time period.&lt;/p&gt;
						&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;img alt=&quot;AWR Reports now available via Performance Hub&quot; moz-do-not-send=&quot;true&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/7364d127a26bef2aef81d19bc431ddf9/awr_report_550.png&quot; /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
						&amp;nbsp;
						
							
								
									LEARN MORE
								
							
						

						
							
								
									
									&lt;div class=&quot;row_set&quot;&gt;
									&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

									&lt;p&gt;DOC: Using Performance Hub to Analyze Database Performance, &lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.cloud.oracle.com/en-us/iaas/Content/Database/Tasks/perfhub.htm&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;

									&lt;p&gt;DOC: Active Session History Reports, &lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/database/oracle/oracle-database/19/tdppt/resolving-transient-performance-problems.html#GUID-7316A970-330C-4F1B-9F9A-7623EFE5B38C&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;

									DO MORE
								
							
						

						
							
								
									
									&lt;div class=&quot;row_set&quot;&gt;
									&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

									&lt;p&gt;DOC: Interpreting Results from Active Session History Reports...&lt;br /&gt;
									After generating an ASH report, you can use the following sections to review its contents to help identify possible causes of transient performance problems:&lt;/p&gt;

									&lt;ul&gt;
										&lt;li&gt;Top Events&lt;/li&gt;
										&lt;li&gt;Top SQL&lt;/li&gt;
										&lt;li&gt;Top PL/SQL&lt;/li&gt;
										&lt;li&gt;Top Sessions&lt;/li&gt;
										&lt;li&gt;Activity Over Time&lt;/li&gt;
									&lt;/ul&gt;

									&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/database/oracle/oracle-database/19/tgdba/analyzing-sampled-data.html#GUID-36ABAF67-227B-4CCA-9B44-F3A87244E7A3&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;

			&lt;a name=&quot;ftl&quot;&gt;&lt;/a&gt;

			
				
					
						
						&lt;div style=&quot;margin-left:10px;&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;Icon for file size increaed when transferring files to OCI Object Store&quot; moz-do-not-send=&quot;true&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/d75f752a236eb0545a8f48d18f202313/gsm_logo1_3664622.png&quot; /&gt;
						&lt;p class=&quot;serverless&quot;&gt;(Shared&lt;br /&gt;
						Infrastructure&lt;br /&gt;
						Only)&lt;/p&gt;
						&lt;/div&gt;
						
						&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;span style=&quot;font-weight:bold; color:red;&quot;&gt;UPDATE &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;feature_header&quot;&gt; - Maximum File Size Increased For Transfer Object Store&lt;/span&gt;
						&lt;p&gt;The maximum file size limit for DBMS_CLOUD.PUT_OBJECT procedure when transferring files to OCI Object Storage has been increased to 50 GB.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Note - there are different size restrictions when using other object stores such as Amazon S3 and Microsoft&amp;#39;s Azure Blob Storage. See doc links below for more details.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
						&amp;nbsp;

						
							
								
									LEARN MORE
								
							
						

						
							
								
									
									&lt;div class=&quot;row_set&quot;&gt;
									&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

									&lt;p&gt;DOC: Details of PUT_OBJECT procedure for ADW, &lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/paas/autonomous-data-warehouse-cloud/user/dbms-cloud.html#GUID-716F0DE7-C669-477E-8AB8-EA42E41ACB12&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;Real Application Security works the same on Autonomous Database as on an on-premise database except you need to perform some additional administrator tasks before using Real Application Security on Autonomous Database. These tasks are now detailed in the documentation.&lt;/p&gt;

        <item>
            <title>Query ORC files and complex data types in Object Storage with Autonomous Database</title>
            <link>https://blogs.oracle.com/datawarehousing/query-orc-files-and-complex-data-types-in-object-storage-with-autonomous-database</link>
            <description>&lt;p&gt;Apache ORC is a columnar file type that is common to the Hadoop ecosystem. &amp;nbsp;It is similar in concept to Apache Parquet; Hortonworks Hadoop clusters often leveraged ORC &amp;ndash; while Cloudera clusters utilized Parquet. &amp;nbsp;Like parquet, ORC is a database file designed for efficient reads. Files embed a schema, data is stored in a compressed columnar format, predicate pushdown enables data pruning &amp;ndash; sound familiar? &amp;nbsp;See the &lt;a href=&quot;https://blogs.oracle.com/datawarehousing/oracle-autonomous-data-warehouse-access-parquet-files-in-object-stores&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Parquet blog post&lt;/a&gt; if you want a refresher :)&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;In addition, ORC provides the ability to capture&amp;nbsp;complex data types &amp;ndash; including arrays, maps, unions and objects (or structs). &amp;nbsp;This capability too is similar to both Parquet and Avro.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Autonomous Database now supports querying object store data that is captured in ORC format &amp;ndash; in addition to text, Avro and Parquet. &amp;nbsp;And, across the structured file types &amp;ndash; you can now also query complex data types. &amp;nbsp;Let&amp;rsquo;s take a look at an example. &amp;nbsp;We&amp;rsquo;ll extend the movie file that was used in our previous Avro post (we downloaded this data from Wikipedia) - this time using the ORC file type with an extra column. The movie file has the following schema:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p style=&quot;margin-left: 40px;&quot;&gt;id int&lt;br /&gt;
original_title string&lt;br /&gt;
overview string&lt;br /&gt;
poster_path string&lt;br /&gt;
release_date string&lt;br /&gt;
vote_count int&lt;br /&gt;
runtime int&lt;br /&gt;
popularity double&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;strong&gt;genres array&amp;lt;struct&amp;lt;id:int,name:string&amp;gt;&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Notice that each movie is categorized by multiple genres (an array of genres). &amp;nbsp;This array is an array of objects - or structs: &amp;nbsp;each genre has an id (integer) and a name (string).&amp;nbsp; Let&amp;#39;s take a look at how to access this data in Autonomous Database.&amp;nbsp; After creating a credential object that enables access to Oracle Object Storage, create a table using dbms_cloud.create_external table:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;begin&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; DBMS_CLOUD.create_credential (&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; credential_name =&amp;gt; &amp;#39;OBJ_STORE_CRED&amp;#39;,&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; username =&amp;gt; abc@oracle.com&amp;#39;,&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; password =&amp;gt; &amp;#39;12345&amp;#39;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; ) ;&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; dbms_cloud.create_external_table (&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; table_name =&amp;gt;&amp;#39;movie_info&amp;#39;,&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; credential_name =&amp;gt;&amp;#39;OBJ_STORE_CRED&amp;#39;,&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; file_uri_list =&amp;gt;&amp;#39;https://objectstorage.us-phoenix-1.oraclecloud.com/n/abcd/b/movies/o/movie-info.orc&amp;#39;,&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; format =&amp;gt; &amp;nbsp;&amp;#39;{&amp;quot;type&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;orc&amp;quot;, &amp;nbsp;&amp;quot;schema&amp;quot;: &amp;quot;first&amp;quot;}&amp;#39;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; );&lt;br /&gt;
end;&lt;br /&gt;
/&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Notice you don&amp;rsquo;t have to specify the shape of the data. &amp;nbsp;The columns and data types are automatically derived by reading the metadata contained in the ORC file. &amp;nbsp;This created a table with the following DDL:&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;CREATE TABLE &amp;quot;ADMIN&amp;quot;.&amp;quot;MOVIE_INFO&amp;quot;&amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;(&amp;nbsp;&amp;quot;ID&amp;quot; NUMBER(10,0),&amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;&amp;quot;ORIGINAL_TITLE&amp;quot; VARCHAR2(4000 BYTE) COLLATE &amp;quot;USING_NLS_COMP&amp;quot;,&amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;&amp;quot;OVERVIEW&amp;quot; VARCHAR2(4000 BYTE) COLLATE &amp;quot;USING_NLS_COMP&amp;quot;,&amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;&amp;quot;POSTER_PATH&amp;quot; VARCHAR2(4000 BYTE) COLLATE &amp;quot;USING_NLS_COMP&amp;quot;,&amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;&amp;quot;RELEASE_DATE&amp;quot; VARCHAR2(4000 BYTE) COLLATE &amp;quot;USING_NLS_COMP&amp;quot;,&amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;&amp;quot;VOTE_COUNT&amp;quot; NUMBER(10,0),&amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;&amp;quot;RUNTIME&amp;quot; NUMBER(10,0),&amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;&amp;quot;POPULARITY&amp;quot; BINARY_DOUBLE,&amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;&amp;quot;GENRES&amp;quot; VARCHAR2(4000 BYTE) COLLATE &amp;quot;USING_NLS_COMP&amp;quot;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;) &amp;nbsp;DEFAULT COLLATION &amp;quot;USING_NLS_COMP&amp;quot;&amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;ORGANIZATION EXTERNAL&amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; ( TYPE ORACLE_BIGDATA&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; DEFAULT DIRECTORY &amp;quot;DATA_PUMP_DIR&amp;quot;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; ACCESS PARAMETERS&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; ( com.oracle.bigdata.credential.name=OBJ_STORE_CRED&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; com.oracle.bigdata.fileformat=ORC&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; )&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; LOCATION&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;( &amp;#39;https://objectstorage.us-phoenix-1.oraclecloud.com/n/abcd/b/movies/o/movie-info.orc&amp;#39;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;)&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; )&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;REJECT LIMIT UNLIMITED&amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; PARALLEL ;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;So, how will you handle the complex data? &amp;nbsp;Simple&amp;hellip; data will be returned as JSON. &amp;nbsp;Thus, despite the fact that different file types store the same data in different ways, your query&amp;nbsp;can be totally agnostic of this fact.&amp;nbsp; You see the same JSON output for all common complex types. &amp;nbsp;Use Oracle&amp;#39;s rich JSON query processing capabilities against the table.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Running a simple query against this table yields the following:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p style=&quot;margin-left: 40px;&quot;&gt;select original_title, release_date, genres&lt;br /&gt;
from movie_info&lt;br /&gt;
where release_date &amp;gt; &amp;#39;2000&amp;#39;&lt;br /&gt;
order by original_title;&lt;/p&gt;


	
		
			original_title
			release_date
			genres
		
	
	
		
			(500) Days of Summer
			2009
			[{&amp;quot;id&amp;quot;:3,&amp;quot;name&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;Drama&amp;quot;},{&amp;quot;id&amp;quot;:6,&amp;quot;name&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;Comedy&amp;quot;},{&amp;quot;id&amp;quot;:17,&amp;quot;name&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;Horror&amp;quot;},{&amp;quot;id&amp;quot;:19,&amp;quot;name&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;Western&amp;quot;},{&amp;quot;id&amp;quot;:18,&amp;quot;name&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;War&amp;quot;},{&amp;quot;id&amp;quot;:15,&amp;quot;name&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;Romance&amp;quot;}]
		
		
			10,000 BC
			2008
			[{&amp;quot;id&amp;quot;:6,&amp;quot;name&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;Comedy&amp;quot;}]
		
		
			11:14
			2003
			[{&amp;quot;id&amp;quot;:9,&amp;quot;name&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;Thriller&amp;quot;},{&amp;quot;id&amp;quot;:14,&amp;quot;name&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;Family&amp;quot;}]
		
		
			127 Hours
			2010
			[{&amp;quot;id&amp;quot;:6,&amp;quot;name&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;Comedy&amp;quot;},{&amp;quot;id&amp;quot;:3,&amp;quot;name&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;Drama&amp;quot;}]
		
		
			13 Going on 30
			2004
			[{&amp;quot;id&amp;quot;:6,&amp;quot;name&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;Comedy&amp;quot;},{&amp;quot;id&amp;quot;:3,&amp;quot;name&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;Drama&amp;quot;},{&amp;quot;id&amp;quot;:18,&amp;quot;name&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;War&amp;quot;},{&amp;quot;id&amp;quot;:15,&amp;quot;name&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;Romance&amp;quot;}]
		
		
			1408
			2007
			[{&amp;quot;id&amp;quot;:45,&amp;quot;name&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;Sci-Fi&amp;quot;},{&amp;quot;id&amp;quot;:6,&amp;quot;name&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;Comedy&amp;quot;},{&amp;quot;id&amp;quot;:17,&amp;quot;name&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;Horror&amp;quot;},{&amp;quot;id&amp;quot;:6,&amp;quot;name&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;Comedy&amp;quot;},{&amp;quot;id&amp;quot;:18,&amp;quot;name&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;War&amp;quot;}]
		
	


&lt;p&gt;Notice that the genres returned as a json array.&amp;nbsp; Let&amp;#39;s make that JSON data more useful.&amp;nbsp; The JSON can be transformed using Oracle&amp;#39;s JSON functions - including the simple &amp;quot;.&amp;quot; notation as well as the more powerful transform functions like JSON_TABLE. &amp;nbsp;The example below queries the table - turning each value of the array into a row in the result set:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p style=&quot;margin-left: 40px;&quot;&gt;select original_title,&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;release_date,&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;m.genre_name,&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;genres&lt;br /&gt;
from movie_info mi,&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;json_table(mi.genres, &amp;#39;$.name[*]&amp;#39;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;COLUMNS (genre_name VARCHAR2(25) PATH &amp;#39;$&amp;#39;) &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; ) AS m&lt;br /&gt;
where rownum &amp;lt; 10;&lt;/p&gt;


	
		
			original_title
			release_date
			genre_name
			genres

&lt;p&gt;JSON_TABLE was used in this case to 1) create a row for each value of the array (think outer join) and 2) the struct was parsed to extract the name of the genre.&lt;/p&gt;

            <guid>https://blogs.oracle.com/datawarehousing/query-orc-files-and-complex-data-types-in-object-storage-with-autonomous-database</guid>
