        <item>
            <title>Oracle Database Vault on Autonomous Database: Quickly and Easily</title>
            <link>https://blogs.oracle.com/datawarehousing/oracle-database-vault-on-autonomous-database%3A-quickly-and-easily</link>
            <description>&lt;p&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;We often talk about how to protect our data from external threats by implementing various practices such as encrypting our data, only allowing connections via TCPS authentication or even further, deploying our databases in a private network. However, these security practices might not be sufficient to eliminate the threats that can originate from unauthorized privileged user access or unauthorized database changes. Good news is that Oracle Database Vault offers comprehensive access control capabilities to prevent those internal threats. What&amp;rsquo;s better is that you can use it in your Oracle Autonomous Database on Shared Exadata Infrastructure (ADB-S) as well! &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;In this blog post, we are going to focus on how to take advantage of Database Vault in ADB-S by just following a few simple steps:&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;ol&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Enable Database Vault &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Control Privileged User Access&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Create a Realm to Protect Your Data&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Disable Database Vault&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ol&gt;

&lt;strong&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Enable Database Vault &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;To configure and enable Oracle Database Vault on Autonomous Database, we will follow the steps described in our &lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/paas/autonomous-data-warehouse-cloud/user/autonomous-database-vault.html#GUID-70F233AF-458F-44B7-9418-F9AF70CFDD15&quot;&gt;documentation&lt;/a&gt;:&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Create two users, one to be the Database Vault owner while the other one to be the Database Vault account manager. This is the first step towards implementing separation of duties.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;


ctuzla$ ./sqlplus ADMIN/************@tuzladv_low

SQL*Plus: Release 19.0.0.0.0 - Production on Wed Jun 3 21:07:29 2020
Version 19.3.0.0.0

Copyright (c) 1982, 2019, Oracle.  All rights reserved.

Last Successful login time: Wed Jun 03 2020 20:55:08 -07:00

Connected to:
Oracle Database 19c Enterprise Edition Release 19.0.0.0.0 - Production
Version 19.5.0.0.0

SQL&amp;gt; create user mydvowner identified by ************;

User created.

SQL&amp;gt; create user mydvacctmgr identified by ************;

User created.


&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Configure Database Vault:&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;


SQL&amp;gt; EXEC DBMS_CLOUD_MACADM.CONFIGURE_DATABASE_VAULT(&amp;#39;mydvowner&amp;#39;, &amp;#39;mydvacctmgr&amp;#39;);

PL/SQL procedure successfully completed.


&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Enable Database Vault:&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;


SQL&amp;gt; EXEC DBMS_CLOUD_MACADM.ENABLE_DATABASE_VAULT;

PL/SQL procedure successfully completed.


&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/paas/autonomous-data-warehouse-cloud/user/autonomous-restart.html#GUID-333DD791-F14C-437C-8B2F-05EF78742493&quot;&gt;Restart&lt;/a&gt;&amp;nbsp;your ADB-s instance.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Confirm Database Vault is enabled:&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;


SQL&amp;gt; SELECT * FROM DBA_DV_STATUS;

NAME		                                 STATUS
------------------   -------------------
DV_APP_PROTECTION    NOT CONFIGURED
DV_CONFIGURE_STATUS  TRUE
DV_ENABLE_STATUS     TRUE


&lt;strong&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Control Privileged User Access&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;In the previous section, we have seen how to set up separate users to be the designated Database Vault owner and account manager. This was an important step in order to achieve separation of duties; however, we are not done yet. In Autonomous Database, &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;ADMIN&lt;/span&gt; user has &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;DV_OWNER&lt;/span&gt; and &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;DV_ACCTMGR&lt;/span&gt; roles by default. What this means is that even after configuring and enabling Database Vault with different users, &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;ADMIN&lt;/span&gt; user can still perform certain operations such user management thanks to these roles. Even though &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;ADMIN&lt;/span&gt; can be considered as a backup account for both Database Vault owner and account manager, it&amp;rsquo;s fairly easy to revoke these roles from &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;ADMIN&lt;/span&gt; as we will see below.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Connect to your ADB-S instance as the designated Database Vault account manager and revoke &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;DV_ACCTMGR&lt;/span&gt; role from &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;ADMIN&lt;/span&gt;:&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;


ctuzla$ ./sqlplus MYDVACCTMGR/************@tuzladv_low

SQL*Plus: Release 19.0.0.0.0 - Production on Wed Jun 3 22:42:00 2020
Version 19.3.0.0.0

Copyright (c) 1982, 2019, Oracle.  All rights reserved.

Last Successful login time: Wed Jun 03 2020 21:18:48 -07:00

Connected to:
Oracle Database 19c Enterprise Edition Release 19.0.0.0.0 - Production
Version 19.5.0.0.0

SQL&amp;gt; revoke dv_acctmgr from ADMIN;

Revoke succeeded.


&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Connect to your ADB-S instance as the designated Database Vault owner and revoke &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;DV_OWNER&lt;/span&gt; role from &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;ADMIN&lt;/span&gt;:&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;


ctuzla$ ./sqlplus MYDVOWNER/************@tuzladv_low

SQL*Plus: Release 19.0.0.0.0 - Production on Wed Jun 3 22:43:30 2020
Version 19.3.0.0.0

Copyright (c) 1982, 2019, Oracle.  All rights reserved.

Last Successful login time: Sun May 31 2020 21:38:21 -07:00

Connected to:
Oracle Database 19c Enterprise Edition Release 19.0.0.0.0 - Production
Version 19.5.0.0.0

SQL&amp;gt; revoke dv_owner from ADMIN;

Revoke succeeded.


&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Confirm &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;ADMIN&lt;/span&gt; user cannot perform any user operations:&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;


ctuzla$ ./sqlplus ADMIN/************@tuzladv_low

SQL*Plus: Release 19.0.0.0.0 - Production on Wed Jun 3 23:00:05 2020
Version 19.3.0.0.0

Connected to:
Oracle Database 19c Enterprise Edition Release 19.0.0.0.0 - Production
Version 19.5.0.0.0

SQL&amp;gt; create user testuser identified by ************;
create user testuser identified by ************
*
ERROR at line 1:
ORA-01031: insufficient privileges


SQL&amp;gt; alter user dvdemo identified by ************;

*

SQL&amp;gt; drop user dvdemo;
drop user dvdemo

&lt;strong&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Create a Realm to Protect Your Data&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;

&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;In this section, we will explore how to create a realm to protect tables of a schema. For this demonstration, I will be using my &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;DVDEMO&lt;/span&gt; schema that contains a table named &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;PRODUCTS&lt;/span&gt;.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;

&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Check if &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;ADMIN&lt;/span&gt; can access the &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;DVDEMO&lt;/span&gt;.&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;PRODUCTS&lt;/span&gt; table:&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;


ctuzla$ ./sqlplus ADMIN/************@tuzladv_low

SQL*Plus: Release 19.0.0.0.0 - Production on Wed Jun 3 23:00:05 2020
Version 19.3.0.0.0

Copyright (c) 1982, 2019, Oracle.  All rights reserved.

Last Successful login time: Wed Jun 03 2020 21:30:55 -07:00

Connected to:
Oracle Database 19c Enterprise Edition Release 19.0.0.0.0 - Production
Version 19.5.0.0.0

SQL&amp;gt; select count(*) from dvdemo.products;

  COUNT(*)
----------
	72


&lt;p style=&quot;margin-left:48px&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;As you can see, &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;ADMIN&lt;/span&gt; can access the data that belongs to another schema since it&amp;rsquo;s not protected by a realm yet.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Create a realm for all tables of the &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;DVDEMO&lt;/span&gt; schema as Database Vault owner:&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;


SQL&amp;gt; begin
  DBMS_MACADM.CREATE_REALM (
    realm_name =&amp;gt; &amp;#39;DVDEMO Realm&amp;#39;,
    description =&amp;gt; &amp;#39;Realm for DVDEMO schema&amp;#39;,
    enabled =&amp;gt; DBMS_MACUTL.G_YES,
    audit_options =&amp;gt; DBMS_MACUTL.G_REALM_AUDIT_OFF,
    realm_type =&amp;gt; 1);
end;
/ 

PL/SQL procedure successfully completed. 

SQL&amp;gt; begin
  DBMS_MACADM.ADD_OBJECT_TO_REALM(
    realm_name =&amp;gt; &amp;#39;DVDEMO Realm&amp;#39;,
    object_owner =&amp;gt; &amp;#39;DVDEMO&amp;#39;,
    object_name =&amp;gt; &amp;#39;%&amp;#39;,
    object_type =&amp;gt; &amp;#39;TABLE&amp;#39;);
end;
/  

PL/SQL procedure successfully completed.


&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Authorize &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;DVDEMO&lt;/span&gt; to access the realm:&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;


SQL&amp;gt; begin
  DBMS_MACADM.ADD_AUTH_TO_REALM(
    realm_name =&amp;gt; &amp;#39;DVDEMO Realm&amp;#39;,
    grantee =&amp;gt; &amp;#39;DVDEMO&amp;#39;,
    auth_options =&amp;gt; DBMS_MACUTL.G_REALM_AUTH_OWNER);
end;
/ 

PL/SQL procedure successfully completed.


&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Try to access &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;PRODUCTS&lt;/span&gt; table as &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;ADMIN&lt;/span&gt; and &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;DVDEMO&lt;/span&gt; users:&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;


ctuzla$ ./sqlplus ADMIN/************@tuzladv_low

SQL*Plus: Release 19.0.0.0.0 - Production on Thu Jun 4 00:04:48 2020
Version 19.3.0.0.0

Copyright (c) 1982, 2019, Oracle.  All rights reserved.

Last Successful login time: Wed Jun 03 2020 23:00:06 -07:00

Connected to:
Oracle Database 19c Enterprise Edition Release 19.0.0.0.0 - Production
Version 19.5.0.0.0

SQL&amp;gt; select count(*) from dvdemo.products;
select count(*) from dvdemo.products
                            *
ERROR at line 1:
ORA-01031: insufficient privileges

ctuzla$ ./sqlplus DVDEMO/************@tuzladv_low

SQL*Plus: Release 19.0.0.0.0 - Production on Thu Jun 4 00:05:44 2020
Version 19.3.0.0.0

Copyright (c) 1982, 2019, Oracle.  All rights reserved.

Last Successful login time: Sun May 31 2020 20:57:16 -07:00

Connected to:
Oracle Database 19c Enterprise Edition Release 19.0.0.0.0 - Production
Version 19.5.0.0.0

SQL&amp;gt; select count(*) from dvdemo.products;

  COUNT(*)
----------
	72


&lt;p style=&quot;margin-left:48px&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;As expected, only &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;DVDEMO&lt;/span&gt; can access the &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;PRODUCTS&lt;/span&gt; table.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;strong&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Disable Database Vault&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;

&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;As the final step, let&amp;rsquo;s take a look at how to disable Database Vault.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;

&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Disable Database Vault using the following API:&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;


ctuzla$ ./sqlplus MYDVOWNER/************@tuzladv_low

SQL*Plus: Release 19.0.0.0.0 - Production on Thu Jun 4 00:13:10 2020
Version 19.3.0.0.0

Copyright (c) 1982, 2019, Oracle.  All rights reserved.

Last Successful login time: Thu Jun 04 2020 00:08:31 -07:00

Connected to:
Oracle Database 19c Enterprise Edition Release 19.0.0.0.0 - Production
Version 19.5.0.0.0

SQL&amp;gt; EXEC DBMS_CLOUD_MACADM.DISABLE_DATABASE_VAULT;

PL/SQL procedure successfully completed.


&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/paas/autonomous-data-warehouse-cloud/user/autonomous-restart.html#GUID-333DD791-F14C-437C-8B2F-05EF78742493&quot;&gt;Restart&lt;/a&gt; your ADB-s instance.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Confirm Database Vault is disabled:&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;


ctuzla$ ./sqlplus ADMIN/************@tuzladv_low

SQL*Plus: Release 19.0.0.0.0 - Production on Thu Jun 4 00:16:50 2020
Version 19.3.0.0.0

Copyright (c) 1982, 2019, Oracle.  All rights reserved.

Last Successful login time: Thu Jun 04 2020 00:04:48 -07:00

Connected to:
Oracle Database 19c Enterprise Edition Release 19.0.0.0.0 - Production
Version 19.5.0.0.0

SQL&amp;gt; SELECT * FROM DBA_DV_STATUS;

NAME		                               STATUS
------------------- --------------------------
DV_APP_PROTECTION   NOT CONFIGURED
DV_CONFIGURE_STATUS TRUE
DV_ENABLE_STATUS    FALSE


&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri,sans-serif&quot;&gt;Check if &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;ADMIN&lt;/span&gt; can access the &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;DVDEMO&lt;/span&gt;.&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;PRODUCTS&lt;/span&gt; table now:&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;


SQL&amp;gt; select count(*) from dvdemo.products;

  COUNT(*)
----------
	72


&lt;p&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:12.0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:&amp;quot;Calibri&amp;quot;,sans-serif&quot;&gt;It is pretty simple, isn&amp;rsquo;t it? In just a few steps, we have gone through how to enable Database Vault, how to limit privileged user access via a realm and how to revert everything back to square one by disabling Database Vault. It&amp;rsquo;s important to note that this is just a small subset of all the capabilities Database Vault offers. If you&amp;rsquo;d like to learn more about Database Vault, please check out &lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/database/oracle/oracle-database/19/dvadm/index.html&quot;&gt;Database Vault Administrator&amp;rsquo;s Guide&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
</description>

			&lt;a name=&quot;ords&quot;&gt;&lt;/a&gt;

			
				
					
						
						&lt;div style=&quot;margin-left:10px;&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;Icon for Oracle REST Data Services&quot; moz-do-not-send=&quot;true&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/7c314c5eb281bdacd2d13ed4f5ea6513/ords_icon.png&quot; /&gt;

						&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;span style=&quot;font-weight:bold; color:red;&quot;&gt;NEW &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;feature_header&quot;&gt; - ADB now supports Customer Managed Oracle REST Data Services&lt;/span&gt;
						&lt;p&gt;When you use the default ORDS on Autonomous Database, you cannot modify any of the ORDS configuration options. For example, with the default configuration connections for ORDS are preconfigured to use the LOW database service.&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;br /&gt;
						You can now use a customer managed environment if you want manual control of the configuration and management of Oracle REST Data Services.&lt;/p&gt;

			&lt;a name=&quot;wmph&quot;&gt;&lt;/a&gt;

			
				
					
						
						&lt;div style=&quot;margin-left:10px;&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;Performance Speedometer Icon&quot; moz-do-not-send=&quot;true&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/7262f9add7a1acfa96751223c00098ab/psb.png&quot; /&gt;
						&lt;p class=&quot;serverless&quot;&gt;(Shared&lt;br /&gt;
						Infrastructure&lt;br /&gt;
						Only)&lt;/p&gt;
						&lt;/div&gt;
						
						&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;span style=&quot;font-weight:bold; color:red;&quot;&gt;NEW &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;feature_header&quot;&gt; - Workload Metrics on Performance Hub&lt;/span&gt;
						&lt;p&gt;Performance Hub has been expanded to include a new tab, &amp;quot;Workload&amp;quot;. This can be used to monitor the workload in the database and helps the user identify performance spikes and bottlenecks.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;There are 4 regions in this tab: CPU Statistics, Wait Time Statistics, Workload Profile, and Sessions. Each region contains a group of charts that indicate the characteristics of the workload and the distribution of the resources, as shown below.&lt;/p&gt;
						&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;img alt=&quot;Autonomous Database Performance Hub console showing new workload metrics&quot; moz-do-not-send=&quot;true&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/4a8e4a66f3bb40e0acc33f54110273f8/perf_hub_workload_500.jpg&quot; /&gt;
						&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;IMAGE - view the screenshot of the new Workload tab containing the four regions and their associated charts are displayed - &lt;a href=&quot;https://einstein.oracle.com/a/yIpElJgQ-8416-mMxVbjPb&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
						&amp;nbsp;

						
							
								
									LEARN MORE

						&lt;a class=&quot;btt&quot; href=&quot;#btt&quot;&gt;BACK TO TOP&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
						&amp;nbsp;
					
				
			
			&lt;a name=&quot;tzs&quot;&gt;&lt;/a&gt;

			
				
					
						
						&lt;div style=&quot;margin-left:10px;&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;Cloud Admin icon&quot; moz-do-not-send=&quot;true&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/0fc248c4f754c74fa282aa6b7bc21c71/ic_developer_female_gray.gif&quot; /&gt;
						&lt;p class=&quot;serverless&quot;&gt;(Shared&lt;br /&gt;
						Infrastructure&lt;br /&gt;
						Only)&lt;/p&gt;
						&lt;/div&gt;
						
						&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;span style=&quot;font-weight:bold; color:red;&quot;&gt;NEW &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;feature_header&quot;&gt; - Performance Hub Now Has a Timezone Selector&lt;/span&gt;
						&lt;p&gt;A time zone control has been added to Performance Hub. This will allow users to view data using an alternate time zone to UTC. They will have the choice of viewing data using either UTC (default), the time zone of their browser client, or the time zone of the database.&lt;/p&gt;
						&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;img alt=&quot;Autonomous Database Performance Hub panel showing new timezone selector&quot; moz-do-not-send=&quot;true&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/749047be6040d82eea048b744e07bda9/per_hub_tz_500.png&quot; /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
						&amp;nbsp;
						&amp;nbsp;
					
				
			

			
				
					
						&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;a class=&quot;btt&quot; href=&quot;#btt&quot;&gt;BACK TO TOP&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
						&amp;nbsp;
					
				
			
			&lt;a name=&quot;nlm&quot;&gt;&lt;/a&gt;

			
				
					
						
						&lt;div style=&quot;margin-left:10px;&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;ADB provides extensions for key IDEs to support common operations&quot; moz-do-not-send=&quot;true&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/0fc248c4f754c74fa282aa6b7bc21c71/ic_developer_female_gray.gif&quot; /&gt;
						&lt;p class=&quot;serverless&quot;&gt;(Shared&lt;br /&gt;
						Infrastructure&lt;br /&gt;
						Only)&lt;/p&gt;
						&lt;/div&gt;
						
						&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;span style=&quot;font-weight:bold; color:red;&quot;&gt;NEW &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;feature_header&quot;&gt; - Latency Metrics Now Available in Service Metrics&lt;/span&gt;
						&lt;p&gt;The Database Service Metrics information help Cloud Admins measure useful quantitative data about their Autonomous Databases. This list of available metrics now includes two new latency metrics:&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;div style=&quot;margin-left:25px&quot;&gt;
						&lt;p&gt;1) Connection latency - Time taken (in milliseconds) to connect to an Autonomous Database that uses shared Exadata infrastructure in each region from a Compute service virtual machine in the same region.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;2) Query latency/response time - Time taken (in milliseconds) to display the results of a simple query on the user&amp;#39;s screen.&lt;/p&gt;
						&lt;/div&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Note - the tests to measure connection latency and query latency are not run against any customer instances.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;Within the Service Metrics console, it is possible to define and publish alarms against these new metrics.&lt;/p&gt;
						&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;img alt=&quot;Service Metrics OCI console showing new latency metrics&quot; moz-do-not-send=&quot;true&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/4a8e4a66f3bb40e0acc33f54110273f8/perf_hub_workload_500.jpg&quot; /&gt;
						&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;IMAGE - view the screenshot of the new latency metrics graphs on Service Metrics console- &lt;a href=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/e890af1af70c746c2d2cd950bfee48a5/latency_metrics_800.png&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
						&amp;nbsp;

						
							
								
									LEARN MORE

			&lt;a name=&quot;tdv&quot;&gt;&lt;/a&gt;

			
				
					
						
						&lt;div style=&quot;margin-left:10px;&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;Cloud Admin icon&quot; moz-do-not-send=&quot;true&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/0fc248c4f754c74fa282aa6b7bc21c71/ic_developer_female_gray.gif&quot; /&gt;
						&lt;p class=&quot;serverless&quot;&gt;(Shared&lt;br /&gt;
						Infrastructure&lt;br /&gt;
						Only)&lt;/p&gt;
						&lt;/div&gt;
						
						&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;span style=&quot;font-weight:bold; color:red;&quot;&gt;NEW &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;feature_header&quot;&gt; - SQL access to tenancy details for ADB&lt;/span&gt;
						&lt;p&gt;When you file a service request for Autonomous Database, you need to provide the tenancy details for your instance. Tenancy details for the instance are available on the Oracle Cloud Infrastructure console. However, if you are connected to the database, you can now obtain these details by querying the &lt;strong&gt;CLOUD_IDENTITY&lt;/strong&gt; column of the &lt;strong&gt;V$PDBS view&lt;/strong&gt;. For example:&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p class=&quot;basic_text&quot; style=&quot;font-family:courier !important; margin-left:40px;&quot;&gt;SELECT cloud_identity&lt;br /&gt;
						FROM v$pdbs;&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;...will generate something similar to the following:&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p class=&quot;basic_text&quot; style=&quot;font-family:courier !important; margin-left:40px;&quot;&gt;{&amp;quot;DATABASE_NAME&amp;quot; : &amp;quot;DBxxxxxxxxxxxx&amp;quot;,&lt;br /&gt;
						&amp;quot;REGION&amp;quot; : &amp;quot;us-phoenix-1&amp;quot;,&lt;br /&gt;
						&amp;quot;TENANT_OCID&amp;quot; : &amp;quot;OCID1.TENANCY.REGION1..ID1&amp;quot;,&lt;br /&gt;
						&amp;quot;DATABASE_OCID&amp;quot; : &amp;quot;OCID1.AUTONOMOUSDATABASE.OC1.SEA.ID2&amp;quot;,&lt;br /&gt;
						&amp;quot;COMPARTMENT_OCID&amp;quot; : &amp;quot;ocid1.tenancy.region1..ID3&amp;quot;}&lt;/p&gt;
						&amp;nbsp;

						
							
								
									LEARN MORE

						&lt;span style=&quot;margin-left:20px; font-size:25pt; line-height:1.5;&quot;&gt;Autonomous Database&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;span style=&quot;margin-left:20px; font-size:15pt; line-height:1.5;&quot;&gt;on Shared Exadata Infrastructure&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;span style=&quot;margin-left:20px; font-size:12pt; line-height:1.5;&quot;&gt;April 30, 2020&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;

						&amp;nbsp;
						&lt;img alt=&quot;ADB Logo&quot; class=&quot;header_icon&quot; moz-do-not-send=&quot;true&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/3171ecca19062436f699f9aedcd05812/adb_header_icon_300.jpeg&quot; style=&quot;margin-top:20px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
						&amp;nbsp;
					
				
			
			&lt;a name=&quot;btt&quot;&gt;&lt;/a&gt;

			
				
					
						
						&lt;div style=&quot;margin-left:20px;&quot;&gt;&amp;nbsp;
						&lt;p&gt;Welcome to our latest customer newsletter for Autonomous Database on Shared Exadata Infrastructure.&amp;nbsp;This newsletter covers the following new features and topics:&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;ul&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;#sla&quot;&gt;Service Level Agreement for ADB&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;#psb&quot;&gt;Per-second billing&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;#soda&quot;&gt;Support for SODA documents and collections&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;#side&quot;&gt;ADB Extensions for IDEs&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;#srs&quot;&gt;Stateful Rule Support in Private Endpoints&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;#dpe&quot;&gt;Enhancements for Data Pump&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;#dwgl&quot;&gt;Global Leaders Program - Update&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;#qle&quot;&gt;Quick Links&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
						&lt;/ul&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;Don&amp;#39;t forget to checkout our &lt;strong&gt;&amp;quot;What&amp;#39;s New&amp;quot;&lt;/strong&gt; page for a comprehensive archive of all the new features we have added to Autonomous Database - &lt;a href=&quot;https://www.oracle.com/database/technologies/datawarehouse-bigdata/adw-features.html&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;To find out how to subscribe to this newsletter &lt;a href=&quot;https://blogs.oracle.com/datawarehousing/announcing-customer-newsletter-for-autonomous-database&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
						&lt;/div&gt;

			&lt;a name=&quot;sla&quot;&gt;&lt;/a&gt;

			
				
					
						
						&lt;div style=&quot;margin-left:10px;&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;Icon for Oracle PaaS and IaaS Public Cloud Services Pillar Document&quot; moz-do-not-send=&quot;true&quot; src=&quot;https://keithlaker.github.io/Publishing/doc-yellow.png&quot; /&gt;
						&lt;p class=&quot;serverless&quot;&gt;(Shared&lt;br /&gt;
						Infrastructure&lt;br /&gt;
						Only)&lt;/p&gt;
						&lt;/div&gt;
						
						&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;span style=&quot;font-weight:bold; color:red;&quot;&gt;NEW &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;feature_header&quot;&gt; - Autonomous Database now comes with an SLA&lt;/span&gt;
						&lt;p&gt;The service level agreement for ADB has just been published and it applies only to the deployment of an Autonomous Database on shared infrastructure.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;The pillar document listed below in the section headed &lt;strong&gt;LEARN&lt;/strong&gt; states that:&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p class=&quot;basic_text&quot; style=&quot;margin-left:30px; margin-right:50px;&quot;&gt;&lt;em&gt;Oracle will use commercially reasonable efforts to have the Oracle Cloud Infrastructure &amp;ndash; Autonomous Database Services on Shared Infrastructure with a Monthly Uptime Percentage of at least 99.95% during any calendar month (the &amp;quot;Service Commitment&amp;quot;). &lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;In the event an Autonomous Database Service on Shared Infrastructure does not meet the &amp;quot;Service Commitment&amp;quot; then customers will be eligible to receive Service Credits. Note - there are specific definitions of key terms in the pillar document (&lt;em&gt;listed below in the section headed &lt;strong&gt;LEARN&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/em&gt;) that you should read and understand.&lt;/p&gt;
						&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;br /&gt;
						&amp;nbsp;
						
							
								
									LEARN MORE
								
							
						

						
							
								
									
									&lt;div class=&quot;row_set&quot;&gt;
									&lt;p&gt;PDF: Oracle PaaS and IaaS Public Cloud Services Pillar Document (April 2020),&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;a href=&quot;https://www.oracle.com/assets/paas-iaas-pub-cld-srvs-pillar-4021422.pdf&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;

									&lt;p&gt;Autonomous Database information is covered in Category 7, which starts on page 4 with ADB covered on pages 17 and 18.&lt;/p&gt;
									&lt;/div&gt;

			&lt;a name=&quot;psb&quot;&gt;&lt;/a&gt;

			
				
					
						
						&lt;div style=&quot;margin-left:10px;&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;Icon showing per second billing for Autonomous Database&quot; moz-do-not-send=&quot;true&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/7262f9add7a1acfa96751223c00098ab/psb.png&quot; /&gt;
						&lt;p class=&quot;serverless&quot;&gt;(Shared&lt;br /&gt;
						Infrastructure&lt;br /&gt;
						Only)&lt;/p&gt;
						&lt;/div&gt;
						
						&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;span style=&quot;font-weight:bold; color:red;&quot;&gt;NEW &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;feature_header&quot;&gt; - Per-Second Billing For Autonomous Database&lt;/span&gt;
						&lt;p&gt;Autonomous Database instance CPU and storage usage is now billed by the second, with a minimum usage period of one minute. Previously Autonomous Database billed in one-hour minimum increments and partial usage of an hour was rounded up to a full hour.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;This change benefits the following types of use cases:&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;ul&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;Where you only run your ADB instances during work hours and stop instances at end of working day&lt;/li&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;Where you start-stop your instances to run overnight batch jobs&lt;/li&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;Where you have ADB instances which typically have a short lifecycle &amp;ndash; sandboxes, QA, training, integration testing instances.&lt;/li&gt;
						&lt;/ul&gt;
						&amp;nbsp;

						
							
								
									LEARN MORE
								
							
						

						
							
								
									
									&lt;div class=&quot;row_set&quot;&gt;
									&lt;p&gt;DOC: Per-second billing announcement for ADW,&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;a class=&quot;doc&quot; href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/paas/autonomous-data-warehouse-cloud/whats-new/index.html&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

									&lt;p&gt;DOC: Per-second billing announcement for ATP,&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;a class=&quot;doc&quot; href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/paas/atp-cloud/atpwn/index.html&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

									&lt;p&gt;DOC: OCI Per-second billing general announcement which covers ADB,&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;a class=&quot;doc&quot; href=&quot;https://docs.cloud.oracle.com/en-us/iaas/Content/Database/Concepts/adboverview.htm#persecondbilling&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

									&lt;p&gt;BLOG: Review of per-second billing on OCI,&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;a class=&quot;doc&quot; href=&quot;https://blogs.oracle.com/cloud-infrastructure/announcing-per-second-billing-for-compute-and-autonomous-database&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
									&lt;/div&gt;
									
								
							
						
						
						&amp;nbsp;
					
				
			

			
				
					
						&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;a class=&quot;btt&quot; href=&quot;#btt&quot;&gt;BACK TO TOP&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
						&amp;nbsp;
					
				
			
			&lt;a name=&quot;soda&quot;&gt;&lt;/a&gt;

			
				
					
						
						&lt;div style=&quot;margin-left:10px;&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;Autonomous Database offers extended support for SODA documents and collections&quot; moz-do-not-send=&quot;true&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/74c05585d162d8b066f67e5710f40956/soda.png&quot; /&gt;
						&lt;p class=&quot;serverless&quot;&gt;(Shared&lt;br /&gt;
						Infrastructure&lt;br /&gt;
						Only)&lt;/p&gt;
						&lt;/div&gt;
						
						&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;span style=&quot;font-weight:bold; color:red;&quot;&gt;NEW &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;feature_header&quot;&gt; - Support for SODA Documents and Collections&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
						&amp;nbsp;
						&lt;p&gt;Autonomous Database now supports loading and using Simple Oracle Document Architecture (SODA) documents and collections. SODA allows developers to store, search, and retrieve document collections, typically JSON documents, without using SQL.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;It is possible to also access document collections with SQL/JSON operators which means that ADB now combines the simplicity of a &lt;em&gt;document database&lt;/em&gt; with the power of a relational database.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;The Oracle Cloud Infrastructure console has been updated with a link to access the SODA drivers for several languages and frameworks including: Java, Node.js, Python, Oracle Call Interface, and PL/SQL, as shown below.&lt;/p&gt;
						&lt;img alt=&quot;Autonomous Database tools panel on OCI console showing access to new SODA drivers&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/9a8055c01a2f6125879db44402e21dcf/tools_soda_500.png&quot; /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
						&amp;nbsp;
						
							
								
									LEARN MORE
								
							
						

						
							
								
									
									&lt;div class=&quot;row_set&quot;&gt;
									&lt;p&gt;DOC: Using JSON Documents with ADW,&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;a class=&quot;doc&quot; href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/paas/autonomous-data-warehouse-cloud/user/document-database.html#GUID-78AA9D61-7370-44D3-BB58-D236FEB19CFB&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

									&lt;p&gt;DOC: Using JSON Documents with ATP,&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;a class=&quot;doc&quot; href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/paas/atp-cloud/atpug/document-database.html#GUID-78AA9D61-7370-44D3-BB58-D236FEB19CFB&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

									&lt;p&gt;Documentation covers the following key topics:&lt;/p&gt;

									&lt;ul&gt;
										&lt;li&gt;Work with Simple Oracle Document Access (SODA) in Autonomous Database&lt;/li&gt;
										&lt;li&gt;SODA Collection Metadata on Autonomous Database&lt;/li&gt;
										&lt;li&gt;Work with JSON Documents Using SQL and PL/SQL APIs on Autonomous Database&lt;/li&gt;
										&lt;li&gt;Load JSON Documents with Autonomous Database&lt;/li&gt;
									&lt;/ul&gt;
									&lt;/div&gt;
									
								
							
						

						&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

						
							
								
									DO MORE
								
							
						

						
							
								
									
									&lt;div class=&quot;row_set&quot;&gt;
									&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

									&lt;p&gt;For examples of using SODA see the following whitepaper:&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;a class=&quot;doc&quot; href=&quot;https://www.oracle.com/technetwork/database/appdev-with-soda-2606220.pdf&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Developing schemaless applications using the Simple Oracle Document Access APIs&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
									&lt;br /&gt;
									&amp;nbsp;&lt;/div&gt;
									
								
							
						
						
						&amp;nbsp;
					
				
			

			
				
					
						&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;a class=&quot;btt&quot; href=&quot;#btt&quot;&gt;BACK TO TOP&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
						&amp;nbsp;
					
				
			
			&lt;a name=&quot;side&quot;&gt;&lt;/a&gt;

			
				
					
						
						&lt;div style=&quot;margin-left:10px;&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;ADB provides extensions for key IDEs to support common operations&quot; moz-do-not-send=&quot;true&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/0fc248c4f754c74fa282aa6b7bc21c71/ic_developer_female_gray.gif&quot; /&gt;
						&lt;p class=&quot;serverless&quot;&gt;(Shared&lt;br /&gt;
						Infrastructure&lt;br /&gt;
						Only)&lt;/p&gt;
						&lt;/div&gt;
						
						&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;span style=&quot;font-weight:bold; color:red;&quot;&gt;NEW &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;feature_header&quot;&gt; - ADB Extensions for IDEs&lt;/span&gt;
						&lt;p&gt;ADB extensions enable developers to connect to, browse, and manage Autonomous Databases directly from their IDEs. There are extensions for the following: Eclipse, Microsoft Visual Studio and Visual Studio Code.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;Users with permissions to manage the databases can perform a number of actions (&lt;em&gt;depending on their IDE&lt;/em&gt;), such as:&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;ul&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;Sign up for Oracle Cloud&lt;/li&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;Connect to a cloud account using a simple auto-generated config file and key file&lt;/li&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;Create new or clone existing Always Free Autonomous Database, Autonomous Database Dedicated, and Autonomous Database Shared databases&lt;/li&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;Automatically download credentials files (including wallets) and quickly connect, browse, and operate on Autonomous Database schemas&lt;/li&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;Change compartments and regions without reconnecting&lt;/li&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;Start, stop, or terminate Autonomous Databases&lt;/li&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;Scale up/down Autonomous Database resources&lt;/li&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;Restore from backup&lt;/li&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;Update instance credentials and/or license type used&lt;/li&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;Rotate wallets&lt;/li&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;Convert Always Free ADBs into paid ADBs&lt;/li&gt;
						&lt;/ul&gt;
						&amp;nbsp;

						
							
								
									LEARN MORE
								
							
						

						
							
								
									
									&lt;div style=&quot;margin-left:300px; margin-right:100px; color:white !important;&quot;&gt;
									&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

									&lt;p&gt;DOC: IDE Extensions in ADW,&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;a class=&quot;doc&quot; href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/paas/autonomous-data-warehouse-cloud/user/develop-with-ide-extensions.html#GUID-35F30F17-26D6-4897-A587-6AB14BB5B68A&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

									&lt;p&gt;DOC: IDE Extensions in ATP,&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;a class=&quot;doc&quot; href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/paas/atp-cloud/atpug/develop-with-ide-extensions.html#GUID-35F30F17-26D6-4897-A587-6AB14BB5B68A&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

			&lt;a name=&quot;srs&quot;&gt;&lt;/a&gt;

			
				
					
						
						&lt;div style=&quot;margin-left:10px;&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;Feature Icon&quot; moz-do-not-send=&quot;true&quot; src=&quot;https://www.oracle.com/ocom/groups/public/@otn/documents/digitalasset/3449984.png&quot; /&gt;
						&lt;p class=&quot;serverless&quot;&gt;(Shared&lt;br /&gt;
						Infrastructure&lt;br /&gt;
						Only)&lt;/p&gt;
						&lt;/div&gt;
						
						&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;span style=&quot;font-weight:bold; color:red;&quot;&gt;NEW &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;feature_header&quot;&gt; - Stateful Rule Support in Private Endpoints&lt;/span&gt;
						&lt;p&gt;When configuring a private endpoint one of the steps is to define a security rule(s) in a Network Security Group. This creates a virtual firewall for the Autonomous Database and allows connections to the Autonomous Database instance.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;The Network Security Group can now be configured with stateful rules.&lt;/p&gt;
						&amp;nbsp;

						
							
								
									LEARN MORE
								
							
						

						
							
								
									
									&lt;div class=&quot;row_set&quot;&gt;
									&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

									&lt;p&gt;DOC: Configure Private Endpoints with ADW, &lt;a class=&quot;doc&quot; href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/paas/autonomous-data-warehouse-cloud/user/access-private-endpoint.html#GUID-2D6A7F84-C7F1-4149-867B-12106F1F7E66&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

									&lt;p&gt;DOC: Configure Private Endpoints with ATP, &lt;a class=&quot;doc&quot; href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/paas/atp-cloud/atpug/access-private-endpoint.html#GUID-2D6A7F84-C7F1-4149-867B-12106F1F7E66&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

									&lt;p&gt;BLOG: Announcing Private Endpoints in Autonomous Database on Shared Exadata Infrastructure, &lt;a class=&quot;doc&quot; href=&quot;https://blogs.oracle.com/datawarehousing/announcing-private-endpoints-in-autonomous-database-on-shared-exadata-infrastructure-v2&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;div style=&quot;margin-left:10px;&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;Enhancements to How Autonomous Database Can Leverage Data Pump Dump Files&quot; moz-do-not-send=&quot;true&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/d75f752a236eb0545a8f48d18f202313/gsm_logo1_3664622.png&quot; /&gt;

						Infrastructure&lt;br /&gt;
						Only)&lt;/p&gt;
						&lt;/div&gt;
						
						&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;span style=&quot;font-weight:bold; color:red;&quot;&gt;UPDATED &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;feature_header&quot;&gt; - Enhancements to Data Pump Support&lt;/span&gt;
						&lt;p&gt;Two specific improvements relating to how Data Pump dump files can be used with ADB. It is now possible to:&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;ul&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;Query Data Pump dump files in the Cloud by creating an external table&lt;/li&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;Use Data Pump dump files in the Cloud as source files to load data&lt;/li&gt;
						&lt;/ul&gt;
						&amp;nbsp;

									&amp;nbsp;

									&lt;p&gt;DOC: Query external Data Pump dump files with ATP, &lt;a class=&quot;doc&quot; href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/paas/atp-cloud/atpug/query-external-data-pump-dump.html#GUID-9BF59C77-20FE-4971-9542-9F26927D89F5&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;Join this Oracle Global Leaders webcast to discover directly from Derek Hayden, SVP, Data Strategy and Analytics at OUTFRONT Media, about the role of Autonomous Data Warehouse in the new data platform for OUTFRONT Media moving in the digital age.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;Derek will discuss initial success with ADW, OAC and how this platform is being used for OUTFRONT&amp;#39;s growth, efficiencies and data management in the out of home advertising industry.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;To register &lt;a href=&quot;https://oracle.zoom.us/webinar/register/WN_6o1rW1NqRA-v_Ru6QEnHeg&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;span style=&quot;font-weight:bold; color:red;&quot;&gt;WEBCAST&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;feature_header&quot;&gt; - Building low code application using Oracle Autonomous Database and Application Express&lt;/span&gt;
						&lt;p&gt;19 May 2020 at 15:00 CET&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;Join this Oracle Global Leaders webcast to discover directly from Dr. Holger Friedrich, CEO, SumIT how they are using Oracle Autonomous Database and the benefit they are getting.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;Oracle Application Express is a powerful low-code web application development framework built-in and ready-to-use with Oracle Autonomous Database. It is instantly available in every provisioned service instance. In this webcast we will explain and demonstrate how sumIT and partner document2relation employ APEX and ATP to provide quick migration services and application development for migrating legacy Lotus Notes applications to the Cloud.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;To register &lt;a href=&quot;https://go.oracle.com/LP=88718?elqCampaignId=236517&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;img moz-do-not-send=&quot;true&quot; src=&quot;http://keithlaker.github.io/Publishing/June_2014.png&quot; /&gt;
						&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;span style=&quot;font-weight:bold; color:red;&quot;&gt;WEBCAST&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;feature_header&quot;&gt; - Smart Shovelling with ADW &amp;amp; APEX&lt;/span&gt;
						&lt;p&gt;13 May 2020 at 12:00 PM ET&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;Join our Global Leaders webinar to hear from Frank Hoogendoorn, CDO of MineSense: a technology solution provider for the Mining Industry that combines IoT and machine learning to create &amp;quot;Smart Shovel&amp;quot; technologies that optimize mine operations, all powered by Oracle solutions!&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;In this Webinar, Frank will explain how MineSense has transitioned from &amp;quot;start-up&amp;quot; to a &amp;quot;scale-up&amp;quot;, and how Autonomous Data Warehouse with built-in APEX is enabling rapid business growth with international Mining customers that include some of the world&amp;rsquo;s largest Copper and Zinc producers. Backed by APEX and ADW, their disruptive &amp;lsquo;smart shovel&amp;rsquo; technology collects and analyzes orebody data in real-time, where machine learning based algorithms drive processing decisions to boost mine productivity while reducing energy consumption, all of which leads to more sustainable mining operations. With the flexibility and low cost setup of ADW, the ease of application development and deployment with APEX, and superb on-demand data processing performance, MineSense will talk about how Oracle Solutions, (some even running right on mining shovels!), have been key in setting up a pivotal digital platform, where IT is no longer seen as a business cost but rather a key driver for growth.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;Don&amp;#39;t forget to checkout our &lt;strong&gt;&amp;quot;What&amp;#39;s New&amp;quot;&lt;/strong&gt; page for a comprehensive archive of all the new features we have added to Autonomous Database - &lt;a href=&quot;https://www.oracle.com/database/technologies/datawarehouse-bigdata/adw-features.html&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;ul&gt;
							&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;#db19&quot;&gt;Options for upgrading to Database 19c&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;

						&amp;nbsp;
					
				
			
			&lt;a name=&quot;db19&quot;&gt;&lt;/a&gt;

			
				
					
						
						&lt;div style=&quot;margin-left:10px;&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;Feature Icon&quot; moz-do-not-send=&quot;true&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/7452caec8faf22b604482d875395e694/19c_logo.png&quot; /&gt;
						&lt;p class=&quot;serverless&quot;&gt;(Shared&lt;br /&gt;
						Infrastructure&lt;br /&gt;
						Only)&lt;/p&gt;
						&lt;/div&gt;
						
						&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;span style=&quot;font-weight:bold; color:red;&quot;&gt;NEW &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;feature_header&quot;&gt; - Upgrade an Autonomous Database Instance to Oracle Database 19c&lt;/span&gt;
						&lt;p&gt;Oracle Database 19c is now available on Autonomous Database for all regions. In select regions, customers can choose between Oracle Database 18c and Oracle Database 19c for new databases. The default version for all new databases is 19c and going forward, most new Autonomous Database features will only be available for databases using Oracle Database 19c.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;Please start planning for the upgrade of your applications to Database 19c. For most applications, there should not be any changes required. However, it is recommended you should test your applications with Database 19c. You can easily test your applications by creating a clone of your current database to Oracle Database 19c, and testing your application using this clone.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;Oracle Database 18c is scheduled to be available in Autonomous Database until September 2020.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;You can choose to upgrade your database at any time during this period. After that time, all existing databases will be automatically upgraded to Oracle Database 19c. There are several approaches to upgrading your database which are described in the documentation, see links below.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Note:&lt;/strong&gt; Autonomous Database plans to offer a new upgrade path starting in April, with a single button that provides a one-way, in-place upgrade.&lt;/p&gt;
						&amp;nbsp;

						
							
								
									LEARN MORE

						&lt;div style=&quot;margin-left:10px;&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;Feature Icon&quot; moz-do-not-send=&quot;true&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/d75f752a236eb0545a8f48d18f202313/gsm_logo1_3664622.png&quot; /&gt;

						Infrastructure&lt;br /&gt;
						Only)&lt;/p&gt;
						&lt;/div&gt;
						
						&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;span style=&quot;font-weight:bold; color:red;&quot;&gt;NEW &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;feature_header&quot;&gt; - Enhancements to Data Pump&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;span class=&quot;feature_header&quot;&gt;1) Support For Pre-Authenticated URLs&lt;/span&gt;
						&lt;p&gt;This enhancement allows Oracle Data Pump to use Oracle Cloud Infrastructure pre-authenticated URIs for source files on Oracle Cloud Infrastructure Object Storage.&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Note&lt;/strong&gt;: Customers should carefully assess the business requirement for and the security ramifications of pre-authenticated access. There is more guidance available in the documentation.&lt;/p&gt;
						&amp;nbsp;

						
							
								
									LEARN MORE
								
							
						

						
							
								
									
									&lt;div style=&quot;margin-left:300px; margin-right:50px; color:white !important;&quot;&gt;

									&lt;p&gt;DOC: Import Data Using Oracle Data Pump on ATP, &lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/paas/atp-cloud/atpug/load-data-data-pump.html#GUID-30DB1EEA-DB45-49EA-9E97-DF49A9968E24&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;click here&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

						Infrastructure&lt;br /&gt;
						Only)&lt;/p&gt;
						&lt;/div&gt;
						
						&lt;br /&gt;
						&lt;span class=&quot;feature_header&quot;&gt;2) Data Pump Export to Object Store&lt;/span&gt;
						&lt;p&gt;It is now possible for Oracle Data Pump to export directly to Oracle Object Store. This simplifies the process of moving data between Autonomous Data Warehouse and other Oracle databases. This export method is supported with Oracle Cloud Infrastructure Object Storage and Oracle Cloud Infrastructure Object Storage Classic.&lt;/p&gt;
						&amp;nbsp;

			&lt;a name=&quot;ocir&quot;&gt;&lt;/a&gt;

						Infrastructure&lt;br /&gt;
						Only)&lt;/p&gt;

						&lt;p&gt;A new menu option has been added to the OCI console to automate the process of stopping and then starting an ADB instance. The new menu option is labelled &amp;quot;Restart&amp;quot; as shown below:&lt;/p&gt;
						   &lt;img srcset=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/45e2c4e7f9b20b4dfa6e0f0557f000ee/ocir_500.png&quot; /&gt; &lt;br /&gt;

						The SSL certificates provided in this wallet will expire on 2025-03-31 21:26:18.928 UTC.&lt;br /&gt;
						In order to avoid any service interruptions due to an expired SSL certificate, you must re-download the wallet before this date.&lt;/p&gt;

            <title>Now Available!  Oracle Big Data Service</title>
            <link>https://blogs.oracle.com/datawarehousing/now-available-oracle-big-data-service</link>
            <description>&lt;div style=&quot;text-align:start; text-indent:0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width:0px&quot;&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:14px&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;caret-color:#ffffff&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;color:#ffffff&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Helvetica&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-style:normal&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-variant-caps:normal&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-weight:normal&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;letter-spacing:normal&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;orphans:auto&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;text-transform:none&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;white-space:normal&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;widows:auto&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;word-spacing:0px&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;-webkit-text-size-adjust:auto&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;text-decoration:none&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:11pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri, sans-serif&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;color:black&quot;&gt;After a successful controlled GA, we are excited to announce general availability for Oracle Big Data Service in the following regions: &amp;nbsp;Ashburn, Sao Paulo, Frankfurt, Tokyo, Seoul, London and Phoenix.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;

&lt;div style=&quot;text-align:start; text-indent:0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width:0px&quot;&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:14px&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;caret-color:#ffffff&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;color:#ffffff&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Helvetica&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-style:normal&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-variant-caps:normal&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-weight:normal&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;letter-spacing:normal&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;orphans:auto&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;text-transform:none&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;white-space:normal&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;widows:auto&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;word-spacing:0px&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;-webkit-text-size-adjust:auto&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;text-decoration:none&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:11pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri, sans-serif&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;color:black&quot;&gt;Oracle Big Data Service is an automated cloud platform service designed&amp;nbsp;for a diverse set of big data use cases and&amp;nbsp;workloads. From agile, short-lived clusters used to tackle specific tasks to long-lived clusters that&amp;nbsp;manage large data&amp;nbsp;lakes, Big Data Service scales to meet all big data&amp;nbsp;requirements at a low cost and with the highest levels of security.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;

&lt;div style=&quot;text-align:start; text-indent:0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width:0px&quot;&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:14px&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;caret-color:#ffffff&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;color:#ffffff&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Helvetica&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-style:normal&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-variant-caps:normal&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-weight:normal&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;letter-spacing:normal&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;orphans:auto&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;text-transform:none&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;white-space:normal&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;widows:auto&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;word-spacing:0px&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;-webkit-text-size-adjust:auto&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;text-decoration:none&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size:11pt&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:Calibri, sans-serif&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;color:black&quot;&gt;Create&amp;nbsp;new big data clusters or efficiently extend your on-premise big data&amp;nbsp;solutions &amp;ndash; and leverage the full capabilities of&amp;nbsp;Cloudera Enterprise Data&amp;nbsp;Hub along with Oracle Big Data analytics capabilities. Take advantage of&amp;nbsp;Oracle Cloud SQL to&amp;nbsp;enable new and existing applications to gain insights&amp;nbsp;from data across the big data landscape using Oracle&amp;rsquo;s advanced&amp;nbsp;SQL&amp;nbsp;dialect &amp;ndash; including data sourced from Hadoop, Object Storage, NoSQL and&amp;nbsp;Kafka. And, use the languages of your&amp;nbsp;choice &amp;ndash; including Python, Scala, R&amp;nbsp;and more &amp;ndash; for machine learning, graph and spatial analytics.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Go to &lt;a href=&quot;https://www.oracle.com/big-data/big-data-service/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Big Data Service&lt;/a&gt; on oracle.com for more information about the new service&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
</description>

            <guid>https://blogs.oracle.com/datawarehousing/now-available-oracle-big-data-service</guid>
            <enclosure>https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/e8f3928c-7512-4a66-82ed-f88dfefaf4c6/File/ef5fb4a172d6864faf26a12dac056f7c/bds_title.png</enclosure>

        <item>
            <title>How to Send an Email using UTL_SMTP in Autonomous Database</title>
            <link>https://blogs.oracle.com/datawarehousing/how-to-send-an-email-using-utl_smtp-in-autonomous-database</link>
            <description>&lt;p&gt;Autonomous Database now supports &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;UTL_HTTP&lt;/span&gt; and &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;UTL_SMTP&lt;/span&gt; PL/SQL packages. You may already be familiar with these as they are commonly used in various scenarios. In this blog post, we will focus on how to send an email using the &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;UTL_SMTP&lt;/span&gt; package. Before we dive into the details, it&amp;#39;s worth noting that both packages are subject to certain restrictions. Even though we&amp;#39;ll cover some of those here, you might still want to see&amp;nbsp;&lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/paas/autonomous-data-warehouse-cloud/user/experienced-database-users.html#GUID-829A7D07-1EA4-4F59-AA60-F780FABAFDEC&quot;&gt;PL/SQL Packages with Restrictions&lt;/a&gt; in the documentation.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;The &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;UTL_SMTP&lt;/span&gt; package&amp;nbsp;is designed for sending emails over Simple Mail Transfer Protocol (SMTP) and it provides numerous interfaces to the SMTP commands (See &lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/database/oracle/oracle-database/18/arpls/UTL_SMTP.html#GUID-F0065C52-D618-4F8A-A361-7B742D44C520&quot;&gt;UTL_SMTP&lt;/a&gt; for more details). Thanks to these interfaces, it&amp;#39;s in fact quite simple to send an email from within the database. However, as mentioned earlier, there are some restrictions that we need to be aware of. For example, the only supported email provider currently is&amp;nbsp;&lt;em&gt;Oracle Cloud Infrastructure (OCI) Email Delivery&lt;/em&gt;&amp;nbsp;service. In other words, we need to have a working Email Delivery configuration before we can start sending emails on Autonomous Database (ADB). Let&amp;#39;s start!&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Here&amp;#39;s the list of steps that we are going to follow to successfully send an email on ADB:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;Configure Email Delivery Service&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;Allow SMTP Access for&amp;nbsp;&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;ADMIN&lt;/span&gt; via an Access Control Entry (ACE)&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;Create a PL/SQL Procedure to Send Email&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;Send a Test Email&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Configure Email Delivery Service&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Oracle Cloud Infrastructure Email Delivery&amp;nbsp;is an email sending service that provides a fast and reliable managed solution for sending high-volume emails&amp;nbsp;(See &lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.cloud.oracle.com/iaas/Content/Email/Concepts/overview.htm&quot;&gt;Overview of the Email Delivery Service&lt;/a&gt; for more details). In this step, we are going to configure Email Delivery in OCI console as shown below:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;Generate SMTP credentials for a user.
	&lt;ul&gt;
		&lt;li&gt;Open the&amp;nbsp;navigation menu. Under&amp;nbsp;&lt;strong&gt;Governance and Administration&lt;/strong&gt;, go to&amp;nbsp;&lt;strong&gt;Identity&lt;/strong&gt;&amp;nbsp;and click&amp;nbsp;&lt;strong&gt;Users&lt;/strong&gt;. Locate the user in the list that has permissions to manage email, and then click the user&amp;#39;s name to view the details.&lt;/li&gt;
		&lt;li&gt;Click&amp;nbsp;&lt;strong&gt;SMTP Credentials&lt;/strong&gt;.&lt;/li&gt;
		&lt;li&gt;Click&amp;nbsp;&lt;strong&gt;Generate SMTP Credentials&lt;/strong&gt;.&lt;/li&gt;
		&lt;li&gt;Enter a&amp;nbsp;&lt;strong&gt;Description&lt;/strong&gt;&amp;nbsp;of the SMTP Credentials in the dialog box.&lt;/li&gt;
		&lt;li&gt;Click&amp;nbsp;&lt;strong&gt;Generate SMTP Credentials&lt;/strong&gt;. A user name and password is displayed.&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;/ul&gt;
	&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;

&lt;p style=&quot;margin-left: 40px;&quot;&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Note:&lt;/strong&gt; Whether you create a new user (See &lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.cloud.oracle.com/iaas/Content/GSG/Tasks/addingusers.htm&quot;&gt;Adding Users&lt;/a&gt;) or choose to use an existing user for these steps, you need to make sure the user is assigned to a group with permissions to manage &lt;em&gt;approved-senders&lt;/em&gt; and &lt;em&gt;suppressions&lt;/em&gt; (See &lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.cloud.oracle.com/iaas/Content/Email/Reference/gettingstarted.htm#permissions&quot;&gt;Set Up Permissions&lt;/a&gt; for more details). For example, our user in this example is assigned to a group that has the following policies for &lt;em&gt;approved-senders&lt;/em&gt; and &lt;em&gt;suppressions&lt;/em&gt;:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p style=&quot;margin-left: 40px;&quot;&gt;Allow group &amp;lt;Your Group Name&amp;gt; to manage approved-senders in tenancy&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p style=&quot;margin-left: 40px;&quot;&gt;Allow group &amp;lt;Your Group Name&amp;gt; to manage suppressions in tenancy&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;Create an approved sender for Email Delivery. We need to do this for all email addresses we use as the &amp;quot;From&amp;quot; with &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;UTL_SMTP.MAIL&lt;/span&gt; (See &lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.cloud.oracle.com/iaas/Content/Email/Tasks/managingapprovedsenders.htm&quot;&gt;Managing Approved Senders&lt;/a&gt;&amp;nbsp;for more information).

	&lt;ul&gt;
		&lt;li&gt;Open the&amp;nbsp;navigation menu. Under&amp;nbsp;&lt;strong&gt;Solutions and Platform&lt;/strong&gt;, go to&amp;nbsp;&lt;strong&gt;Email Delivery&lt;/strong&gt;&amp;nbsp;and click&amp;nbsp;&lt;strong&gt;Email Approved Senders&lt;/strong&gt;.&lt;/li&gt;
		&lt;li&gt;Click&amp;nbsp;&lt;strong&gt;Create Approved Sender&lt;/strong&gt;&amp;nbsp;within the&amp;nbsp;&lt;strong&gt;Approved Senders&lt;/strong&gt;&amp;nbsp;view.&lt;/li&gt;
		&lt;li&gt;Enter the email address you want to list as an approved sender in the&amp;nbsp;&lt;strong&gt;Create Approved Sender&lt;/strong&gt;&amp;nbsp;dialog box.&lt;/li&gt;
		&lt;li&gt;Click&amp;nbsp;&lt;strong&gt;Create Approved Sender&lt;/strong&gt;. The email address is added to your Approved Senders list.&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;/ul&gt;
	&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Allow SMTP Access for&amp;nbsp;ADMIN via an Access Control Entry (ACE)&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Now we need to append an access control entry (ACE) using the &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;DBMS_NETWORK_ACL_ADMIN&lt;/span&gt; package for &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;ADMIN&lt;/span&gt; user to access SMTP for a specific host&amp;nbsp;and port:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Note:&lt;/strong&gt; You can find your SMTP endpoint (host) and eligible ports by opening&amp;nbsp;the&amp;nbsp;navigation menu following&amp;nbsp;&lt;strong&gt;Email Delivery &lt;/strong&gt;--&amp;gt; &lt;strong&gt;Email Configuration&lt;/strong&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;


begin
  -- Allow SMTP access for user ADMIN
  dbms_network_acl_admin.append_host_ace(
    host =&amp;gt;&amp;#39;smtp.us-ashburn-1.oraclecloud.com&amp;#39;,
    lower_port =&amp;gt; 587,
    upper_port =&amp;gt; 587,
    ace =&amp;gt; xs$ace_type(
      privilege_list =&amp;gt; xs$name_list(&amp;#39;SMTP&amp;#39;),
    principal_name =&amp;gt; &amp;#39;ADMIN&amp;#39;,
    principal_type =&amp;gt; xs_acl.ptype_db));
end;
/ 


&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Create a PL/SQL Procedure to Send Email&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/p&gt;


CREATE OR REPLACE PROCEDURE SEND_MAIL (
  msg_to varchar2,
  msg_subject varchar2,
  msg_text varchar2 ) 
IS

  mail_conn utl_smtp.connection;
  username varchar2(1000):= &amp;#39;ocid1.user.oc1.username&amp;#39;;
  passwd varchar2(50):= &amp;#39;password&amp;#39;;
  msg_from varchar2(50) := &amp;#39;adam@example.com&amp;#39;;
  mailhost VARCHAR2(50) := &amp;#39;smtp.us-ashburn-1.oraclecloud.com&amp;#39;;

BEGIN
  mail_conn := UTL_smtp.open_connection(mailhost, 587);
  utl_smtp.starttls(mail_conn);
  
  UTL_SMTP.AUTH(mail_conn, username, passwd, schemes =&amp;gt; &amp;#39;PLAIN&amp;#39;);
  
  utl_smtp.mail(mail_conn, msg_from);
  utl_smtp.rcpt(mail_conn, msg_to);
  
  UTL_smtp.open_data(mail_conn);
 
  UTL_SMTP.write_data(mail_conn, &amp;#39;Date: &amp;#39; || TO_CHAR(SYSDATE, &amp;#39;DD-MON-YYYY HH24:MI:SS&amp;#39;) || UTL_TCP.crlf);
  UTL_SMTP.write_data(mail_conn, &amp;#39;To: &amp;#39; || msg_to || UTL_TCP.crlf);
  UTL_SMTP.write_data(mail_conn, &amp;#39;From: &amp;#39; || msg_from || UTL_TCP.crlf);
  UTL_SMTP.write_data(mail_conn, &amp;#39;Subject: &amp;#39; || msg_subject || UTL_TCP.crlf);
  UTL_SMTP.write_data(mail_conn, &amp;#39;Reply-To: &amp;#39; || msg_to || UTL_TCP.crlf || UTL_TCP.crlf);
  UTL_SMTP.write_data(mail_conn, msg_text || UTL_TCP.crlf || UTL_TCP.crlf);
  
  UTL_smtp.close_data(mail_conn);
  UTL_smtp.quit(mail_conn);

EXCEPTION
  WHEN UTL_smtp.transient_error OR UTL_smtp.permanent_error THEN
    UTL_smtp.quit(mail_conn);
    dbms_output.put_line(sqlerrm);
  WHEN OTHERS THEN
    UTL_smtp.quit(mail_conn);
    dbms_output.put_line(sqlerrm);
END;
/


&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Notes&lt;/strong&gt;:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;&lt;em&gt;username&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;: Specifies the SMTP credential username.&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;&lt;em&gt;passwd&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;: Specifies the SMTP credential password.&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;&lt;em&gt;msg_from&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;: Specifies one of the approved senders.&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;&lt;em&gt;mailhost&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;: Specifies the SMTP connection endpoint.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Send a Test Email&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;In order to verify that we configured everything accurately and created a working&amp;nbsp;procedure (&lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;SEND_MAIL&lt;/span&gt;), we will send a test email:&lt;/p&gt;


execute send_mail(&amp;#39;taylor@example.com&amp;#39;, &amp;#39;Email from Oracle Autonomous Database&amp;#39;, &amp;#39;Sent using UTL_SMTP&amp;#39;);



&lt;p&gt;To summarize, UTL_SMTP package is now supported in Autonomous Database and we just explored how to send an email by taking advantage of this package&amp;nbsp;the OCI Email Delivery service. If you&amp;#39;d like to learn more about Email Delivery or &lt;span style=&quot;font-family:'Courier New'&quot;&gt;UTL_SMTP&lt;/span&gt; in ADB, please follow the documentation links referenced above.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;
</description>

Just in case you missed it: the console&amp;nbsp;has been updated with the addition of a new &lt;strong&gt;Tools&lt;/strong&gt; tab alongside the existing tabs for &amp;quot;&lt;strong&gt;Information&lt;/strong&gt;&amp;quot; and &amp;quot;&lt;strong&gt;Tags&lt;/strong&gt;&amp;quot;.&lt;/p&gt;
