        <item>
            <title>Is your data in parts and lying in other object stores? No worries, Autonomous Database has you ...</title>
            <link>https://blogs.oracle.com/datawarehousing/creating-partitioned-external-tables-over-any-object-store</link>
            <description>&lt;p style=&quot;text-align: center;&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/f3971c04-8bd4-4efa-a5e3-1af82fc8a9ca/Image/93c7477a629fdecdb18b4dc4d607bdaa/table_row_detailed.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 400px; height: 312px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Whether you personally believe in the multi-cloud lifestyle that&amp;rsquo;s in vogue or not, the reality is you may be dealing with different departments or orgs within your company that store their data in their cloud&amp;nbsp;of choice,&amp;nbsp;and partitioned in various ways. Autonomous DB&amp;nbsp;doesn&amp;#39;t judge, we&amp;nbsp;support&amp;nbsp;querying or ingesting your data whether it lies in Oracle Cloud&amp;nbsp;Object Store, Azure, or AWS!&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Let me walk you through a simple example of how you may query your multi-part data lying in any of these&amp;nbsp;object stores. We will be using the &lt;u&gt;new&amp;nbsp;partitioned&amp;nbsp;external table&lt;/u&gt; functionality in the DBMS_CLOUD&amp;nbsp;package, which creates&amp;nbsp;a&amp;nbsp;partitioned&amp;nbsp;table structure over flat files lying in your external storage. (ie. a query on this table fetches data directly from&amp;nbsp;the flat files in external storage, instead of the database&amp;#39;s own&amp;nbsp;datafiles).&amp;nbsp;You may use the other&amp;nbsp;functions in this package&amp;nbsp;if you need to apply this&amp;nbsp;to a&amp;nbsp;&lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/paas/autonomous-data-warehouse-cloud/user/dbms-cloud.html#GUID-2AFBEFA4-992E-4F53-96DB-F560084C7DA9&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;non-partitioned external table&lt;/a&gt;, or to actually &lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/paas/autonomous-data-warehouse-cloud/user/dbms-cloud.html#GUID-9428EA51-5DDD-43C2-B1F5-CD348C156122&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;copy data&lt;/a&gt; into your database.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Let&amp;#39;s begin with&amp;nbsp;some cloud concepts we will be using further in the post:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;In general, an &lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.cloud.oracle.com/iaas/Content/Object/Concepts/objectstorageoverview.htm&quot; style=&quot;color:#0563c1; text-decoration:underline&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Object Store&lt;/a&gt; is a cloud-based, scalable, serverless storage platform that offers storage of &amp;ldquo;objects&amp;rdquo;. These objects can be unstructured data of any content type, including analytic data and rich content, like images and videos. Oracle&amp;rsquo;s Object Storage, AWS S3 and Azure Blob Storage are all examples of object stores.&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;A private object store URL is a URL that requires authentication via a credential to be accessed.&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;Pre-Authenticated URLs and Public URLs don&amp;rsquo;t require any credentials to be accessed. Having the complete URL will give&amp;nbsp;someone access to that data.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Next,&amp;nbsp;&lt;strong&gt;download&amp;nbsp;&lt;/strong&gt;the 2 part&amp;nbsp;file in a zip&amp;nbsp;&lt;a href=&quot;https://app.compendium.com/api/post_attachments/9b9078fe-7784-4acf-bf9b-2563ee08367f/view&quot;&gt;here&lt;/a&gt;. In keeping with some of my previous posts, we will use&amp;nbsp;the small weather history&amp;nbsp;data set from Charlotte, NC in Comma Separated Values (CSV) format. The file which has&amp;nbsp;&amp;quot;Part 1&amp;quot; in its name has July 2014 weather data, and that with &amp;quot;Part 2&amp;quot; will be the following month&amp;rsquo;s, Aug 2014&amp;nbsp;weather data.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Now&amp;nbsp;&lt;strong&gt;select the cloud object store&lt;/strong&gt;&amp;nbsp;that you will be using to jump to the appropriate section:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;a id=&quot;allobjectstores&quot; name=&quot;allobjectstores&quot;&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p style=&quot;text-align: center;&quot;&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;#oracleobjectstore&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/f3971c04-8bd4-4efa-a5e3-1af82fc8a9ca/Image/730eac0386d359af35f69d35bf1db62f/oracle_cloud.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 150px; height: 86px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;img alt=&quot;Image result for line&quot; src=&quot;http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-c9t3e2loGvw/UTauw-ej5xI/AAAAAAAAAEQ/7L7VOv27n5I/s1600/vrline21.jpg&quot; style=&quot;height: 60px; width: 60px;&quot; /&gt; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;a href=&quot;#azure&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/f3971c04-8bd4-4efa-a5e3-1af82fc8a9ca/Image/5d2a964a11c009e63f5944820b601e79/azure.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 150px; height: 64px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&amp;nbsp;.&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;&lt;img alt=&quot;Image result for line&quot; src=&quot;http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-c9t3e2loGvw/UTauw-ej5xI/AAAAAAAAAEQ/7L7VOv27n5I/s1600/vrline21.jpg&quot; style=&quot;height: 60px; width: 60px;&quot; /&gt; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;a href=&quot;#aws&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/f3971c04-8bd4-4efa-a5e3-1af82fc8a9ca/Image/ffe9de4d21423fc8d94e0704ee6ed5c0/amazon_s3_icon_1.jpg&quot; style=&quot;width: 150px; height: 113px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;


&lt;a name=&quot;oracleobjectstore&quot;&gt;&lt;/a&gt;Using Oracle Cloud Object Storage

&amp;nbsp;

Step 1: Unzip and upload&amp;nbsp;the two downloaded files&amp;nbsp;to your Oracle Cloud Object Storage&amp;nbsp;bucket

&lt;p&gt;Create an Object Store bucket and unzip&amp;nbsp;and upload the two Weather history files to your object store. You can refer to &lt;a href=&quot;https://oracle.github.io/learning-library/workshops/journey4-adwc/?page=LabGuide3.md&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;this hands-on lab&lt;/a&gt;&amp;nbsp;for a detailed walkthrough of&amp;nbsp;how to do this in your&amp;nbsp;Oracle Cloud tenancy.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p style=&quot;text-align: center;&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/f3971c04-8bd4-4efa-a5e3-1af82fc8a9ca/Image/3dd7bc95ec29e144b1a402025e2b2fb8/oci_object_storage.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 1000px; height: 905px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p style=&quot;text-align: center;&quot;&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Keep note of the &amp;quot;Visibility&amp;quot; (you can use&amp;nbsp;Private or Public)&amp;nbsp;of the bucket to which&amp;nbsp;you are uploading the files. This will come in handy in Step 3.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p style=&quot;text-align: center;&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/f3971c04-8bd4-4efa-a5e3-1af82fc8a9ca/Image/54402d5bfc40a164bfb3ce1a7e14ccd5/public_private.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 1000px; height: 482px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p style=&quot;text-align: center;&quot;&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

Step 2: Create a credential to access your object store for your Private URLs

&lt;p&gt;Dive into SQL Developer that is &lt;a href=&quot;https://oracle.github.io/learning-library/workshops/journey4-adwc/?page=LabGuide1.md&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;connected to your Autonomous Database&lt;/a&gt;,&amp;nbsp;and create a credential for your object store like below. The&amp;nbsp;username&amp;nbsp;is your Oracle Cloud Infrastructure username. The&amp;nbsp;password&amp;nbsp;is your Oracle Cloud Infrastructure&amp;nbsp;generated auth token:&lt;/p&gt;
BEGIN&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; DBMS_CLOUD.CREATE_CREDENTIAL (&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; credential_name =&amp;gt; &amp;#39;OBJ_STORE_CRED&amp;#39;,&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; username =&amp;gt; &amp;#39;&amp;lt;OCI username&amp;gt;&amp;#39;,&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; password =&amp;gt; &amp;#39;&amp;lt;OCI auth token&amp;gt;&amp;#39;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; );&lt;br /&gt;
END;&lt;br /&gt;
/ 

&lt;p&gt;Note: If you are unsure about how to create an auth token, refer to Step 8 in in the same&amp;nbsp;&lt;a href=&quot;https://oracle.github.io/learning-library/workshops/journey4-adwc/?page=LabGuide3.md&quot;&gt;lab tutorial&lt;/a&gt; mentioned above. While we have used&amp;nbsp;a&amp;nbsp;username and password for simplicity here, we recommend&amp;nbsp;that you use &lt;a href=&quot;https://blogs.oracle.com/datawarehousing/autonomous-database-now-supports-accessing-the-object-storage-with-oci-native-authentication&quot;&gt;native authentication&lt;/a&gt;&amp;nbsp;for your production systems added security and versatility.&lt;/p&gt;

&amp;nbsp;

Step 3: Create a&amp;nbsp;Partitioned External Table on top of your two-part Weather History data

&lt;p&gt;Now that we have a credential ready, run the PL/SQL script below using your Object Store URLs in the &lt;em&gt;&lt;strong&gt;location&lt;/strong&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/em&gt;parameters.&amp;nbsp;You may either construct the URLs yourself by &lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/paas/autonomous-data-warehouse-cloud/user/file-uri-formats.html#GUID-5D3E1614-ADF2-4DB5-B2B2-D5613F10E4FA&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;looking at this&amp;nbsp;URL&amp;nbsp;format&lt;/a&gt;&amp;nbsp;or find the URL from the details of your file in the object store console as in the following screens.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p style=&quot;text-align: center;&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/f3971c04-8bd4-4efa-a5e3-1af82fc8a9ca/Image/ae4b45253df0a36f0767b265e3ed3647/object_details.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 1000px; height: 507px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p style=&quot;text-align: center;&quot;&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p style=&quot;text-align: center;&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/f3971c04-8bd4-4efa-a5e3-1af82fc8a9ca/Image/8cdeb69cbf717c5fe37053363ee58dac/oci_url_path.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 1000px; height: 441px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Since we have a month&amp;#39;s worth of data in each file, we call the DBMS_CLOUD.CREATE_EXTERNAL_PART_TABLE function to create the partitioned external&amp;nbsp;table with 2 partitions using the &lt;strong&gt;REPORT_DATE column&lt;/strong&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Note:&amp;nbsp;We are using a credential&amp;nbsp;parameter in this call to DBMS_CLOUD to illustrate the use of&amp;nbsp;files that lie in a&amp;nbsp;private object storage&amp;nbsp;bucket (ie. that have private URLs). If we use public bucket or&amp;nbsp;pre-authenticated URLs, we can omit the credential parameter entirely. We can also use a mix of private and public URLs from the same object store if required.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;
BEGIN&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp;DBMS_CLOUD.CREATE_EXTERNAL_PART_TABLE( &amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp;table_name =&amp;gt;&amp;#39;WEATHER_REPORT_EXTERNAL_PART&amp;#39;, &amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp;credential_name =&amp;gt;&amp;#39;OBJ_STORE_CRED&amp;#39;, &amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp;format =&amp;gt; json_object(&amp;#39;type&amp;#39; value &amp;#39;csv&amp;#39;, &amp;#39;skipheaders&amp;#39; value &amp;#39;1&amp;#39;,&amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&amp;#39;dateformat&amp;#39; value &amp;#39;mm/dd/yy&amp;#39;),&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; column_list =&amp;gt; &amp;#39;REPORT_DATE DATE, &amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;ACTUAL_MEAN_TEMP NUMBER, &amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;ACTUAL_MIN_TEMP NUMBER, &amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; ACTUAL_MAX_TEMP NUMBER, &amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;AVERAGE_MIN_TEMP NUMBER, &amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; AVERAGE_MAX_TEMP NUMBER, &amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;AVERAGE_PRECIPITATION NUMBER&amp;#39;,&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; partitioning_clause =&amp;gt;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;#39;partition by range (REPORT_DATE)&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; (partition p1 values less than (to_date(&amp;#39;&amp;#39;01-AUG-2014&amp;#39;&amp;#39;,&amp;#39;&amp;#39;DD-MON-YYYY&amp;#39;&amp;#39;)) &lt;strong&gt;location&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; ( &amp;#39;&amp;#39;https://objectstorage.us-ashburn-1.oraclecloud.com/&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; n/adwctraining5/b/partitiontest/o/Charlotte_NC_Weather_History_Part1.csv&amp;#39;&amp;#39;)&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;,&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;partition p2 values less than (to_date(&amp;#39;&amp;#39;01-SEP-2014&amp;#39;&amp;#39;,&amp;#39;&amp;#39;DD-MON-YYYY&amp;#39;&amp;#39;)) &lt;strong&gt;location&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; ( &amp;#39;&amp;#39;https://objectstorage.us-ashburn-1.oraclecloud.com/&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; n/adwctraining5/b/partitiontest/o/Charlotte_NC_Weather_History_Part2.csv&amp;#39;&amp;#39;)&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;)&amp;#39; &amp;nbsp; );&lt;br /&gt;
END;&lt;br /&gt;
/ 

&amp;nbsp;

&lt;a href=&quot;#end&quot;&gt;&amp;darr; Click here to Jump to Step 4&lt;/a&gt;&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;|&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;a ebates-serp-link=&quot;title&quot; href=&quot;#allobjectstores&quot; ping=&quot;/url?sa=t&amp;amp;source=web&amp;amp;rct=j&amp;amp;url=https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%25E2%2586%2591&amp;amp;ved=2ahUKEwj_7JOxvurlAhVRsp4KHYpzB4AQFjAJegQIAhAB&quot;&gt;Click here to Jump to object store selection&lt;/a&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;a ebates-serp-link=&quot;title&quot; href=&quot;#allobjectstores&quot; ping=&quot;/url?sa=t&amp;amp;source=web&amp;amp;rct=j&amp;amp;url=https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%25E2%2586%2591&amp;amp;ved=2ahUKEwj_7JOxvurlAhVRsp4KHYpzB4AQFjAJegQIAhAB&quot;&gt;&amp;uarr; &lt;/a&gt;


&amp;nbsp;

&lt;a id=&quot;azure&quot; name=&quot;azure&quot;&gt;&lt;/a&gt;Using Microsoft Azure Blob Storage

&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

Step 1: Unzip and upload&amp;nbsp;the two downloaded files&amp;nbsp;to your Azure Blob Storage container

&lt;p&gt;Navigate to your Azure Blob Storage account, create a container and&amp;nbsp;unzip&amp;nbsp;and upload the two Weather history files. (Refer to &lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/storage/blobs/storage-quickstart-blobs-portal&quot;&gt;these detailed steps&lt;/a&gt;&amp;nbsp;on&amp;nbsp;how to do this if necessary).&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p style=&quot;text-align: center;&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/f3971c04-8bd4-4efa-a5e3-1af82fc8a9ca/Image/e25253770e24ebf8332d8b0993c27266/azure_blob.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 1000px; height: 372px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p style=&quot;text-align: center;&quot;&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Keep note of the &amp;quot;Access Level&amp;quot; of your container (you can use a Private or Public container) in which you uploaded&amp;nbsp;the files. This will come in handy in Step 3.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p style=&quot;text-align: center;&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/f3971c04-8bd4-4efa-a5e3-1af82fc8a9ca/Image/e95912d88d428498278eb4d122a68b69/private_azure.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 1000px; height: 550px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&amp;nbsp;

Step 2: Create a credential to access your Blob&amp;nbsp;storage&amp;nbsp;for your Private URLs

&lt;p&gt;Dive&amp;nbsp;into SQL Developer that is &lt;a href=&quot;https://oracle.github.io/learning-library/workshops/journey4-adwc/?page=LabGuide1.md&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;connected to your Autonomous Database&lt;/a&gt;,&amp;nbsp;and create a credential for your blob&amp;nbsp;store like below. The&amp;nbsp;username&amp;nbsp;is your Azure Storage account name. The&amp;nbsp;password&amp;nbsp;is your Azure storage account access key:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;BEGIN&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; DBMS_CLOUD.CREATE_CREDENTIAL (&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; credential_name =&amp;gt; &amp;#39;OBJ_STORE_CRED&amp;#39;,&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; username =&amp;gt; &amp;#39;&amp;lt;Azure Storage account name&amp;gt;&amp;#39;,&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; password =&amp;gt; &amp;#39;&amp;lt;Azure Storage account access key&amp;gt;&amp;#39;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; );&lt;br /&gt;
END;&lt;br /&gt;
/ &lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p style=&quot;text-align: center;&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/f3971c04-8bd4-4efa-a5e3-1af82fc8a9ca/Image/0ef6e990d2de8178477ece29f73a1cfe/access_key.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 1000px; height: 758px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Note: If you are still unsure about how to find your Azure&amp;nbsp;storage account access key, follow detailed steps &lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/storage/common/storage-account-manage?toc=%2fazure%2fstorage%2fblobs%2ftoc.json&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;

&amp;nbsp;

Step 3: Create a&amp;nbsp;Partitioned External Table on top of your two-part Weather History data

&lt;p&gt;Now that we have a credential ready, run the PL/SQL script below using your Azure Blob store URLs in the &lt;em&gt;&lt;strong&gt;location&lt;/strong&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/em&gt;parameters.&amp;nbsp;You may either construct the URLs yourself by &lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/paas/autonomous-data-warehouse-cloud/user/file-uri-formats.html#GUID-5D3E1614-ADF2-4DB5-B2B2-D5613F10E4FA&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;looking at the URL&amp;nbsp;format&lt;/a&gt;&amp;nbsp;or find the URL from the details of your file in the blob&amp;nbsp;store console as in the following screen:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p style=&quot;text-align: center;&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/f3971c04-8bd4-4efa-a5e3-1af82fc8a9ca/Image/6f940666bc550bc8c419d3208ff02e3c/azure_file_url.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 1000px; height: 566px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p style=&quot;text-align: center;&quot;&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Since we have a month&amp;#39;s worth of data in each file, we call the DBMS_CLOUD.CREATE_EXTERNAL_PART_TABLE function to create the partitioned external&amp;nbsp;table with 2 partitions using the &lt;strong&gt;REPORT_DATE column&lt;/strong&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Note:&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;
	&lt;p&gt;We are using a credential&amp;nbsp;parameter in this call to DBMS_CLOUD to illustrate the use of&amp;nbsp;files that lie in a&amp;nbsp;private Azure blob storage&amp;nbsp;container (ie. that have private URLs). If we use a &lt;u&gt;public access container&lt;/u&gt;, we can omit the credential parameter entirely. We can also use a mix of private and public URLs from the same object store if required.&lt;/p&gt;
	&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;
	&lt;p&gt;We don&amp;#39;t currently support pre-authenticated URLs for&amp;nbsp;Azure,&amp;nbsp;that&amp;#39;s coming soon. Feel free to comment below if your business relies heavily on this.&lt;/p&gt;
	&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;
BEGIN&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp;DBMS_CLOUD.CREATE_EXTERNAL_PART_TABLE( &amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp;table_name =&amp;gt;&amp;#39;WEATHER_REPORT_EXTERNAL_PART&amp;#39;, &amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp;credential_name =&amp;gt;&amp;#39;OBJ_STORE_CRED&amp;#39;, &amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp;format =&amp;gt; json_object(&amp;#39;type&amp;#39; value &amp;#39;csv&amp;#39;, &amp;#39;skipheaders&amp;#39; value &amp;#39;1&amp;#39;,&amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&amp;#39;dateformat&amp;#39; value &amp;#39;mm/dd/yy&amp;#39;),&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; column_list =&amp;gt; &amp;#39;REPORT_DATE DATE, &amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;ACTUAL_MEAN_TEMP NUMBER, &amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;ACTUAL_MIN_TEMP NUMBER, &amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; ACTUAL_MAX_TEMP NUMBER, &amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;AVERAGE_MIN_TEMP NUMBER, &amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; AVERAGE_MAX_TEMP NUMBER, &amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;AVERAGE_PRECIPITATION NUMBER&amp;#39;,&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; partitioning_clause =&amp;gt;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;#39;partition by range (REPORT_DATE)&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; (partition p1 values less than (to_date(&amp;#39;&amp;#39;01-AUG-2014&amp;#39;&amp;#39;,&amp;#39;&amp;#39;DD-MON-YYYY&amp;#39;&amp;#39;)) &lt;strong&gt;location&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; ( &amp;#39;&amp;#39;https://nilaysobjectstore.blob.core.windows.net/&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; externaltest/Charlotte_NC_Weather_History_Part1.csv&amp;#39;&amp;#39;)&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;,&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;partition p2 values less than (to_date(&amp;#39;&amp;#39;01-SEP-2014&amp;#39;&amp;#39;,&amp;#39;&amp;#39;DD-MON-YYYY&amp;#39;&amp;#39;)) &lt;strong&gt;location&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; ( &amp;#39;&amp;#39;https://nilaysobjectstore.blob.core.windows.net/&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; externaltest/Charlotte_NC_Weather_History_Part2.csv&amp;#39;&amp;#39;)&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;)&amp;#39; &amp;nbsp; );&lt;br /&gt;
END;&lt;br /&gt;
/ 

&amp;nbsp;

&lt;a href=&quot;#end&quot;&gt;&amp;darr; Click here to Jump to Step 4&lt;/a&gt;&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;|&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;a ebates-serp-link=&quot;title&quot; href=&quot;#allobjectstores&quot; ping=&quot;/url?sa=t&amp;amp;source=web&amp;amp;rct=j&amp;amp;url=https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%25E2%2586%2591&amp;amp;ved=2ahUKEwj_7JOxvurlAhVRsp4KHYpzB4AQFjAJegQIAhAB&quot;&gt;Click here to Jump to object store selection&lt;/a&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;a ebates-serp-link=&quot;title&quot; href=&quot;#allobjectstores&quot; ping=&quot;/url?sa=t&amp;amp;source=web&amp;amp;rct=j&amp;amp;url=https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%25E2%2586%2591&amp;amp;ved=2ahUKEwj_7JOxvurlAhVRsp4KHYpzB4AQFjAJegQIAhAB&quot;&gt;&amp;uarr;&lt;/a&gt;


&amp;nbsp;

&lt;a id=&quot;aws&quot; name=&quot;aws&quot;&gt;&lt;/a&gt;Using AWS S3 Storage

&amp;nbsp;

Step 1: Unzip and upload&amp;nbsp;the two downloaded files&amp;nbsp;to your AWS S3 Storage container

&lt;p&gt;Navigate to your AWS S3 storage account, create a bucket and&amp;nbsp;unzip&amp;nbsp;and upload the two Weather history files. (Refer to &lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.aws.amazon.com/vsts/latest/userguide/s3-upload.html&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;these detailed steps&lt;/a&gt;&amp;nbsp;on&amp;nbsp;how to do this if necessary).&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p style=&quot;text-align: center;&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/f3971c04-8bd4-4efa-a5e3-1af82fc8a9ca/Image/3161930dd0a52322ffdf82bba181f4a8/aws_s3_bucket.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 1000px; height: 528px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p style=&quot;text-align: center;&quot;&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Keep note of the Permissions&amp;nbsp;of your bucket (you can use a Private or Public access) in which you uploaded&amp;nbsp;the files. This will come in handy in Step 3.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p style=&quot;text-align: center;&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/f3971c04-8bd4-4efa-a5e3-1af82fc8a9ca/Image/27a23d7dbfed2639923bcbf1483277a0/aws_public_access.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 1000px; height: 500px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&amp;nbsp;

Step 2: Create a credential to access your AWS S3 storage&amp;nbsp;for your Private URLs

&lt;p&gt;Dive into SQL Developer that is &lt;a href=&quot;https://oracle.github.io/learning-library/workshops/journey4-adwc/?page=LabGuide1.md&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;connected to your Autonomous Database&lt;/a&gt;,&amp;nbsp;and create a credential for your S3 store&amp;nbsp;like below. The&amp;nbsp;username&amp;nbsp;is your AWS Access key ID. The&amp;nbsp;password&amp;nbsp;is your AWS secret access key:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;BEGIN&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; DBMS_CLOUD.CREATE_CREDENTIAL (&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; credential_name =&amp;gt; &amp;#39;OBJ_STORE_CRED&amp;#39;,&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; username =&amp;gt; &amp;#39;&amp;lt;AWS Access key ID&amp;gt;&amp;#39;,&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; password =&amp;gt; &amp;#39;&amp;lt;AWS secret access key&amp;gt;&amp;#39;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; );&lt;br /&gt;
END;&lt;br /&gt;
/ &lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Note: If you are still unsure about how to find your AWS access key ID and&amp;nbsp;secret access key, follow detailed steps &lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.aws.amazon.com/IAM/latest/UserGuide/id_credentials_access-keys.html#Using_CreateAccessKey&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;

&amp;nbsp;

Step 3: Create a&amp;nbsp;Partitioned External Table on top of your two-part Weather History data

&lt;p&gt;Now that we have a credential ready, run the PL/SQL script below using your AWS S3&amp;nbsp;URLs in the &lt;em&gt;&lt;strong&gt;location&lt;/strong&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/em&gt;parameters.&amp;nbsp;You may either construct the URLs yourself by &lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/paas/autonomous-data-warehouse-cloud/user/file-uri-formats.html#GUID-5D3E1614-ADF2-4DB5-B2B2-D5613F10E4FA&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;looking at the URL&amp;nbsp;format&lt;/a&gt;&amp;nbsp;or find the URL from the details of your file in the S3 bucket&amp;nbsp;console as in the following screen:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p style=&quot;text-align: center;&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/f3971c04-8bd4-4efa-a5e3-1af82fc8a9ca/Image/dedea9ca2e1eb3e1c46a022b2a394781/aws_url.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 1000px; height: 492px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p style=&quot;text-align: center;&quot;&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Since we have a month&amp;#39;s worth of data in each file,&amp;nbsp;we call the DBMS_CLOUD.CREATE_EXTERNAL_PART_TABLE function to create the partitioned external&amp;nbsp;table with 2 partitions using the &lt;strong&gt;REPORT_DATE column&lt;/strong&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Note:&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;
	&lt;p&gt;We are using a credential&amp;nbsp;parameter in this call to DBMS_CLOUD to illustrate the use of&amp;nbsp;files that lie in a&amp;nbsp;private AWS S3 storage bucket&amp;nbsp;(ie. that have private URLs). If we use a &lt;u&gt;public access bucket&lt;/u&gt;, we can omit the credential parameter entirely. We can also use a mix of private and public URLs from the same object store if required.&lt;/p&gt;
	&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;
	&lt;p&gt;We don&amp;#39;t currently support pre-authenticated URLs for AWS, but that&amp;#39;s coming&amp;nbsp;soon. Feel free to comment below if your business relies heavily on this.&lt;/p&gt;
	&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;
BEGIN&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp;DBMS_CLOUD.CREATE_EXTERNAL_PART_TABLE( &amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp;table_name =&amp;gt;&amp;#39;WEATHER_REPORT_EXTERNAL_PART&amp;#39;, &amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp;credential_name =&amp;gt;&amp;#39;OBJ_STORE_CRED&amp;#39;, &amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp;format =&amp;gt; json_object(&amp;#39;type&amp;#39; value &amp;#39;csv&amp;#39;, &amp;#39;skipheaders&amp;#39; value &amp;#39;1&amp;#39;,&amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&amp;#39;dateformat&amp;#39; value &amp;#39;mm/dd/yy&amp;#39;),&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; column_list =&amp;gt; &amp;#39;REPORT_DATE DATE, &amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;ACTUAL_MEAN_TEMP NUMBER, &amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;ACTUAL_MIN_TEMP NUMBER, &amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; ACTUAL_MAX_TEMP NUMBER, &amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;AVERAGE_MIN_TEMP NUMBER, &amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; AVERAGE_MAX_TEMP NUMBER, &amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;AVERAGE_PRECIPITATION NUMBER&amp;#39;,&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; partitioning_clause =&amp;gt;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;#39;partition by range (REPORT_DATE)&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; (partition p1 values less than (to_date(&amp;#39;&amp;#39;01-AUG-2014&amp;#39;&amp;#39;,&amp;#39;&amp;#39;DD-MON-YYYY&amp;#39;&amp;#39;)) &lt;strong&gt;location&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;(&amp;#39;&amp;#39;https://nilaystests.s3-us-west-1.amazonaws.com/Charlotte_NC_Weather_History_Part1.csv&amp;#39;&amp;#39;)&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;,&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;partition p2 values less than (to_date(&amp;#39;&amp;#39;01-SEP-2014&amp;#39;&amp;#39;,&amp;#39;&amp;#39;DD-MON-YYYY&amp;#39;&amp;#39;)) &lt;strong&gt;location&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;(&amp;#39;&amp;#39;https://nilaystests.s3-us-west-1.amazonaws.com/Charlotte_NC_Weather_History_Part2.csv&amp;#39;&amp;#39;)&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;)&amp;#39; &amp;nbsp; );&lt;br /&gt;
END;&lt;br /&gt;
/


&lt;p&gt;&lt;a id=&quot;end&quot; name=&quot;end&quot;&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

Step 4: Validate and Query your data

&lt;p&gt;We&amp;#39;re done already! You may run the &amp;quot;DBMS_CLOUD.VALIDATE_EXTERNAL_TABLE&amp;quot; function to validate that your partitioned external table was created correctly and can access its underlying data. (Validation is an optional but recommended step)&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp; EXEC DBMS_CLOUD.VALIDATE_EXTERNAL_TABLE(&amp;#39;WEATHER_REPORT_EXTERNAL_PART&amp;#39;);&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;If things went awry and&amp;nbsp;you receive&amp;nbsp;an error, you may look at the logfile and badfile to easily troubleshoot any errors you see. (Refer to &lt;a href=&quot;http://EXEC DBMS_CLOUD.VALIDATE_EXTERNAL_TABLE('WEATHER_REPORT_EXTERNAL_PART');&quot;&gt;this&amp;nbsp;lab tutorial&amp;#39;s Step 12&lt;/a&gt;&amp;nbsp;for more detail on this).&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;If you sailed&amp;nbsp;through with no errors, you may now query&amp;nbsp;the table as a whole or by partition&amp;nbsp;(ie. in this case, by month) with the script below.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Notice that in the third query&amp;nbsp;we select data &lt;em&gt;between&lt;/em&gt; July 5th and 21st 2014, all of which lies in partition P1. This query therefore makes use of the performance&amp;nbsp;benefits of partitioned external tables,&amp;nbsp;and only needs to physically access the file named &amp;quot;Part 1&amp;quot; file under the hood!&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;
SELECT REPORT_DATE, AVERAGE_PRECIPITATION FROM WEATHER_REPORT_EXTERNAL_PART;&lt;br /&gt;
SELECT REPORT_DATE, AVERAGE_MIN_TEMP FROM WEATHER_REPORT_EXTERNAL_PART PARTITION (P2); SELECT * FROM WEATHER_REPORT_EXTERNAL_PART where REPORT_DATE between &amp;#39;05-JUL-2014&amp;#39; and &amp;#39;21-JUL-2014&amp;#39;;&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;

&lt;p style=&quot;text-align: center;&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/f3971c04-8bd4-4efa-a5e3-1af82fc8a9ca/Image/3baf50418d261191d8abbc26331451d5/screen_shot_2019_11_14_at_1_13_21_pm.png&quot; style=&quot;height: 574px; width: 1000px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;So, there you&amp;nbsp;have it! Autonomous Database aims to not only simplify the provisioning and management of your&amp;nbsp;database in the cloud, but also aims&amp;nbsp;to provide&amp;nbsp;easy to use functions to make your entire interaction with the database&amp;nbsp;seamless and intuitive.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;a ebates-serp-link=&quot;title&quot; href=&quot;#allobjectstores&quot; ping=&quot;/url?sa=t&amp;amp;source=web&amp;amp;rct=j&amp;amp;url=https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%25E2%2586%2591&amp;amp;ved=2ahUKEwj_7JOxvurlAhVRsp4KHYpzB4AQFjAJegQIAhAB&quot;&gt;&amp;uarr; Click here to jump back&amp;nbsp;to object store selection to try a different one&lt;/a&gt;
</description>

        <item>
            <title>Keeping Your Autonomous Data Warehouse Secure with Data Safe - Part 2</title>
            <link>https://blogs.oracle.com/datawarehousing/keeping-your-autonomous-data-warehouse-secure-with-data-safe-part-2</link>
            <description>
	
		
			&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/14149a08-b73e-4069-a85d-b10b09770f02/File/f9184ce338f1cd44bae4ed9d87269439/data_safe_image_blog_1_.jpg&quot; style=&quot;width: 549px; height: 309px;&quot; /&gt;
		
	


&lt;p&gt;In the part 1 of this series we looked at how to get your ADW and OCI environment ready for using Data Safe. If you missed part 1 or need a quick refresher then the blog post is here:&amp;nbsp;&lt;a href=&quot;https://blogs.oracle.com/datawarehousing/keeping-your-autonomous-data-warehouse-secure-with-data-safe-part-1&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;https://blogs.oracle.com/datawarehousing/keeping-your-autonomous-data-warehouse-secure-with-data-safe-part-1&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;In this post we are going to explore the process of connecting and Autonomous Data Warehouse instance to our newly deployed Data Safe environment. Remember that you deploy your Data Safe control center within a specific OCI regional data center - &lt;em&gt;as is the case with all our other cloud services. &lt;/em&gt;Therefore, if you switch to a different data center then you will need to deploy a new&amp;nbsp;Data Safe environment. Hope that makes sense!&lt;/p&gt;

Launching the Data Safe Service Console

&lt;p&gt;In part 1 we got to the point of enabling Data Safe in the Frankfurt data center. Now when we login to Oracle Cloud using our newly created OCI credentials we can pop open the hamburger menu and select Data Safe:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/75048be8f6ae938c050069215b3bdd58/screen_shot_2019_11_06_at_14_24_37.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 295px; height: 517px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;and arrive on the Data Safe landing pad. The next step is to launch the Service Console (you may be wondering...why doesn&amp;#39;t the Service Console just open automatically since the landing pad page is empty, apart from the Service Console button! Great question and we will come back to this towards the end of the series of posts when the landing pad page will show a lot&amp;nbsp;more information).&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;After clicking on the&amp;nbsp;Service Console button a new window pops open which looks like this:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/5bbc70d7e069067bec37ef15c243dc68/screen_shot_2019_11_06_at_14_23_11.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 549px; height: 309px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Right now, there is no information showing on any of our graphs or any of the other pages. This is because we have not registered&amp;nbsp;our data warehouse instance so that&amp;#39;s the next step.&lt;/p&gt;

Registering an ADW with Data Safe

&lt;p&gt;We need to register our ADW with Data Safe&amp;nbsp;before we can generate any of the&amp;nbsp;reports that are part of the&amp;nbsp;Data Safe library. To do that we need to go to the tab marked &amp;quot;Target&amp;quot; in the horizontal menu at the top of the page:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/1e003040d7347cf3dadc655dc043f92e/screen_shot_2019_11_06_at_14_39_45.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 550px; height: 309px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Clicking on the &amp;quot;Register&amp;quot; button will pop open a form where we can input the connection details for our ADW...&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/39cf9d1a7b418a2dbabd3e5fd14ab371/screen_shot_2019_11_06_at_14_43_08.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 549px; height: 309px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Data Safe is not limited to just working with Autonomous Databases and&amp;nbsp;we&amp;nbsp;could register any of the following:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/77768f9e045464b0e814a6a0daeb2cd8/screen_shot_2019_11_06_at_14_46_20.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 552px; height: 122px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;span&gt;Nnote that &lt;/span&gt;Data Safe supports only serverless deployments for Autonomous Database. &amp;quot;Dedicated&amp;quot; is not currently supported. There is more information here:&amp;nbsp;&lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/paas/data-safe/udscs/supported-target-databases.html&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/paas/data-safe/udscs/supported-target-databases.html&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;For ADW (and ATP) we first need to change the connection type to TLS which will add some additional fields to the form - &lt;em&gt;this will be most recognisable if you have been&amp;nbsp;spent time configuring connections to ADW from DI/ETL or BI tools&lt;/em&gt;:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/e74877f4c464d7338b82b0aa0b1864b7/screen_shot_2019_11_06_at_14_49_29.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 549px; height: 309px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;it looks as if a lot of information is now&amp;nbsp;required to register our ADW instance but the good news is that just about all the information we need is contained within a small zip file which we can download from our OCI ADB console. Essentially we need the wallet file for our instance. But first let&amp;#39;s quickly complete the fields in the top part of the form:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/ca4ea1e31dd2de865970842305292886/screen_shot_2019_11_06_at_15_00_06.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 550px; height: 309px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Ok, now we need the information about our ADW instance and here&amp;#39;s how you get it:&lt;/p&gt;

Collecting Connection Information For ADW

&lt;p&gt;If we flip over to the OCI console page for our ADW instance we can see that there is a line for something called &amp;quot;&lt;strong&gt;OCID&lt;/strong&gt;&amp;quot; which is the first piece of information we need to collect .There are two links next to it: &amp;quot;Show&amp;quot; and &amp;quot;Copy&amp;quot;.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/4c2f09017b030baa777e34b500a1868c/screen_shot_2019_11_06_at_14_54_41.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 549px; height: 309px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Click on copy and then flip over to our Data Safe page and paste in the OCID reference. Now we need things like hostname, port, service name and target distinguished name along with various secure wallet files. To get this information we need to download the wallet file which can be accessed by clicking on the &amp;quot;DB Connection&amp;quot; button. On the pop-up form click the &amp;quot;Download Wallet&amp;quot; button and enter a password...note this down because we are going to need it again shortly...&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/040b95fa0d3e04b2db09d4ecd18c0dd8/screen_shot_2019_11_06_at_14_54_50.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 549px; height: 309px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Once the file has been downloaded, find the file on your filesystem and unzip it. The result will be a&amp;nbsp;folder containing the following files:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/ba2414ccb7c6502109f66e84aa3b76db/screen_shot_2019_11_06_at_15_08_20.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 203px; height: 172px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Ok, back to our Target registration form on Data Safe....the data for the next four fields can all be found in the tnsnames.ora file. We are going to use the &amp;quot;low service&amp;quot; for this connection because running Data Safe reports is not an urgent, rush-rush, workload.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p style=&quot;margin-left: 40px;&quot;&gt;&lt;i&gt;If you have no idea what a &amp;quot;low service&amp;quot; is then it might be a good idea to quickly read through the section on &amp;quot;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://docs.oracle.com/en/cloud/paas/autonomous-data-warehouse-cloud/user/manage-priorities.html#GUID-80E464A7-8ED4-45BB-A7D6-E201DD4107B7&quot; style=&quot;font-style: italic;&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Managing Concurrency and Priorities on Autonomous Data Warehouse&lt;/a&gt;&lt;i&gt;&amp;quot; in section 12 of the ADW documentation. In simple terms...when we&amp;nbsp;connect to an ADW instance we need to&amp;nbsp;select a service (low, medium or high).&amp;nbsp;These services map to LOW, MEDIUM, and HIGH consumer&amp;nbsp;groups which have the following&amp;nbsp;characteristics:&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;ul style=&quot;margin-left: 40px;&quot;&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;em&gt;HIGH: Highest resources, lowest concurrency. Queries run in parallel.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;em&gt;MEDIUM: Fewer resources, higher concurrency. Queries run in parallel.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;em&gt;LOW: Least resources, highest concurrency. Queries run serially.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Anyway....as long as the jobs run, then we are going to be happy. Therefore, we need to find the details for our &lt;strong&gt;low-service connection&lt;/strong&gt;&amp;nbsp;in the tnsnames.ora file which will look something like this:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p style=&quot;font-family: courier;&quot;&gt;adwdemo_low = (description=(address=(protocol=tcps)(port=1522)(host=xxxxxx.oraclecloud.com))(connect_data=(service_name=xxxxx_adwdemo_low.xxxxxxx))(security=(ssl_server_cert_dn=&amp;quot;CN=xxxxxx.oraclecloud.com,OU=Oracle,O=Oracle Corporation,L=Redwood&amp;nbsp;City,ST=California,C=US&amp;quot;)))&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;You can copy &amp;amp; paste the host, port, service_name and&amp;nbsp;ssl_server_cert_dn into the four fields below the &amp;quot;TLS&amp;quot; pulldown menu entry. So now our form looks like this...&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/7e5f96b862938c546328c1272141898b/screen_shot_2019_11_06_at_15_17_53.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 549px; height: 309px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;now the last few steps....make sure the wallet type is set to &amp;quot;JKS Wallet&amp;quot;. For the Certificate/Wallet find the &amp;quot;truststore.jks&amp;quot; file from our downloaded and unzipped connection file. In the same directory/folder we can pick &amp;quot;keystone.jks&amp;quot; for the &amp;quot;Keystore Wallet&amp;quot;. The next field needs the password we used on the OCI ADW console page when we downloaded the connection zip file so paste that in...&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Lastly add the ADW instance username/password that we created in&amp;nbsp;Part 1of this series of blog posts&amp;nbsp;- our user was called&amp;nbsp;DATASAFE.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/1af497aea197e15ab4bfdfddf4b5b65b/screen_shot_2019_11_06_at_15_34_33.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 550px; height: 215px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;before you click on the &amp;quot;Test Connection&amp;quot; button we need to run a PL/SQL script to give our new DATASAFE database user some privileges that will allow Data Safe to run though it&amp;#39;s library of checks...&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/b056eeffc6c9e8839bf40b4adf9e85bc/screen_shot_2019_11_06_at_15_40_48.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 550px; height: 50px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Click on the download button then search for the&amp;nbsp;PL/SQL script dscs_privileges.sql. Using SQL Developer (or any other tool) we need to login as our standard ADMIN user and run that script (copy &amp;amp; paste will do the trick). Check the log for the script and you should see something like this:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p style=&quot;margin-left: 40px; font-family:courier;&quot;&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
Enter value for USERNAME (case sensitive matching the username from dba_users)&lt;br /&gt;
Setting USERNAME to DATASAFE&lt;br /&gt;
Enter value for TYPE (grant/revoke)&lt;br /&gt;
Setting TYPE to GRANT&lt;br /&gt;
Enter value for MODE (audit_collection/audit_setting/data_discovery/masking/assessment/all)&lt;br /&gt;
Setting MODE to ALL&lt;br /&gt;
Granting AUDIT_COLLECTION privileges to &amp;quot;DATASAFE&amp;quot; ...&amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;
Granting AUDIT_SETTING privileges to &amp;quot;DATASAFE&amp;quot; ...&amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;
Granting DATA_DISCOVERY role to &amp;quot;DATASAFE&amp;quot; ...&amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;
Granting MASKING role to &amp;quot;DATASAFE&amp;quot; ...&amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;
Granting ASSESSMENT role to &amp;quot;DATASAFE&amp;quot; ...&amp;nbsp;&lt;br /&gt;
Done.&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;br /&gt;
Disconnected from Oracle Database 18c Enterprise Edition Release 18.0.0.0.0 - Production&lt;br /&gt;
Version 18.4.0.0.0&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;NOW, we can test the connection... and everything should work and we should&amp;nbsp;see a nice big green tick.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/c91ae6f4ba783f410ec1f1c8a4ac40cd/screen_shot_2019_11_06_at_15_33_37.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 549px; height: 309px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;div&gt;Finally we are ready to click on &amp;quot;Register Target&amp;quot;. Now our target page shows the details of our newly registered database...&lt;/div&gt;

&lt;div&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/div&gt;

&lt;div&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/581c0377839490d7388a060c5f64eb95/screen_shot_2019_11_06_at_15_46_30.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 549px; height: 309px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;

&lt;div&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/div&gt;

&lt;div&gt;Of course that&amp;#39;s all we have done - register our ADW as a new target - so all the other pages are still empty, including the home page:&lt;/div&gt;

&lt;div&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/div&gt;

&lt;div&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;https://cdn.app.compendium.com/uploads/user/e7c690e8-6ff9-102a-ac6d-e4aebca50425/3f1f9085-e459-4b23-85f7-ed09e21ffb29/Image/bedde041e097a107c72d0b5673457bf6/screen_shot_2019_11_06_at_15_49_27.png&quot; style=&quot;width: 549px; height: 309px;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;

&lt;div&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/div&gt;

Wrap up for Part 2

&lt;div&gt;In part 1 we setup our environment ready for using Data Safe and we enabled Data Safe within our regional data center - in this case the Frankfurt Data Center. In this post, Part 2, we have successfully added our existing ADW instance as a new target database in Data Safe.&lt;/div&gt;

&lt;div&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/div&gt;

Coming up in Part 3

&lt;div&gt;In the next post we will start to explore some of the data discovery and data masking features that are part of Data Safe.&lt;/div&gt;

&lt;div&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/div&gt;
